      <b>
       Munich
      </b>
      (
      <span class="nowrap">
       <span class="IPA nopopups">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
         /
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">

          </span>

          </span>
         </span>
         /
        </a>
       </span>
      </span>
      ; also
      <span class="nowrap">
       <span class="IPA nopopups">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">
         /
         <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
          <span title="// primary stress follows">
           
          </span>
          <span title="'m' in 'my'">
           m
          </span>
          <span title="/ju/ long 'u' in 'cute'">
           ju
          </span>

       </span>
      </span>
      in UK English;
      <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
       German
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="de">
       <i>
        Mnchen
       </i>
      </span>
      ,
      <small>
       pronounced
      </small>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_German" title="Help:IPA for German">
        [mnn]
       </a>
      </span>
      <small class="nowrap metadata">
       (
       <a href="/wiki/File:De-M%C3%BCnchen.ogg" title="File:De-Mnchen.ogg">
        <img alt="" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="13" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" width="13"/>
       </a>
       <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/De-M%C3%BCnchen.ogg" title="De-Mnchen.ogg">
        listen
       </a>
       )
      </small>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_language" title="Bavarian language">
       Bavarian
      </a>
      :
      <span lang="bar">
       <i>
        Minga
       </i>
      </span>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       [m()]
      </span>
      ) is the capital and largest city of the
      <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">
       German
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">
       state
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">
       Bavaria
      </a>
      , on the banks of River
      <a href="/wiki/Isar" title="Isar">
       Isar
      </a>
      north of the
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Limestone_Alps" title="Northern Limestone Alps">
       Bavarian Alps
      </a>
      . Munich is the
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Germany_by_population" title="List of cities in Germany by population">
       third largest city
      </a>
      in Germany, after
      <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
       Berlin
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">
       Hamburg
      </a>
      , with a population of around 1.5million.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Metropolitan_Region" title="Munich Metropolitan Region">
       Munich Metropolitan Region
      </a>
      is home to 5.8 million people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The name of the city is derived from the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">
       Old
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Middle_High_German" title="Middle High German">
       Middle High German
      </a>
      term
      <i>
       Munichen
      </i>
      , meaning "by the monks". It derives from the monks of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictine_order" title="Benedictine order">
       Benedictine order
      </a>
      who ran a monastery at the place that was later to become the Old Town of Munich; hence the monk depicted on
      <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Munich" title="Coat of arms of Munich">
       the city's coat of arms
      </a>
      . Munich was first mentioned in 1158. From 1255 the city was seat of the
      <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">
       Bavarian Dukes
      </a>
      . Black and gold  the colours of the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
       Holy Roman Empire
      </a>
       have been the city's official colours since the time of
      <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Louis IV, Holy Roman Emperor">
       Ludwig the Bavarian
      </a>
      , when it was an imperial residence. Following a final reunification of the
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wittelsbach" title="House of Wittelsbach">
       Wittelsbachian
      </a>
      Duchy of Bavaria, previously divided and sub-divided for more than 200 years, the town became the country's sole capital in 1506. Catholic Munich was a cultural stronghold of the
      <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">
       Counter-Reformation
      </a>
      and a political point of divergence during the resulting
      <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">
       Thirty Years' War
      </a>
      , but remained physically untouched despite an occupation by the Protestant
      <a href="/wiki/Swedes" title="Swedes">
       Swedes
      </a>
      ; as the townsfolk would rather open the gates of their town than risk siege and almost inevitable destruction
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      . Like wide parts of the
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">
       Holy Roman Empire
      </a>
      , the area recovered slowly economically. Having evolved from a duchy's capital into that of an
      <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">
       electorate
      </a>
      (1623), and later a sovereign
      <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">
       kingdom
      </a>
      (1806), Munich has been a centre of arts, culture and science since the early 19th century. The city became the Nazi movement's infamous
      <i>
       Hauptstadt der Bewegung
      </i>
      (lit.: "Capital of the movement"), and after post-war reconstruction was the host city of the
      <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">
       1972 Summer Olympics
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Munich is home to many national and international authorities, major universities, major museums and theaters. Its numerous architectural attractions, international sports events, exhibitions, conferences and
      <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">
       Oktoberfest
      </a>
      attract considerable
      <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">
       tourism
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since 2006, the city's
      <a href="/wiki/Motto" title="Motto">
       motto
      </a>
      has been "
      <i>
       <span lang="de">
        Mnchen mag dich
       </span>
      </i>
      " ("Munich loves you").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Munich is a traffic hub with excellent international, national and local connections, running a fast and reliable public transport system. It is a centre of finance, publishing and advanced technologies. Munich is one of the most prosperous and fastest growing cities in Germany, and the seat of numerous corporations and insurance companies. It is a top-ranked destination for migration and expatriate location, despite being the municipality with the highest density of population (4,500 inh. per km) in Germany. Munich achieved fourth place in the frequently quoted
      <a href="/wiki/Mercer_Quality_of_Living_Survey" title="Mercer Quality of Living Survey">
       Mercer livability rankings
      </a>
      in 2011
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For economic and social innovation, the city was ranked 15th globally out of 289 cities in 2010, and 5th in Germany by the 2thinknow Innovation Cities Index based on analysis of 162 indicators.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2013,
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monocle_(2007_magazine)" title="Monocle (2007 magazine)">
        Monocle
       </a>
      </i>
      ranked Munich as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World%27s_most_livable_cities" title="World's most livable cities">
       world's most livable city
      </a>
      with the highest quality of life.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Munich" title="History of Munich">
       History of Munich
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Munich" title="Timeline of Munich">
       Timeline of Munich
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="376" data-file-width="496" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg/220px-Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg/330px-Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg/440px-Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Germany_M%C3%BCnchen_Monks.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Munich city
        <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Munich" title="Coat of arms of Munich">
         coat of arms
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Origin_as_medieval_town">
       Origin as medieval town
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origin as medieval town">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The year 1158 is assumed to be the foundation date, which is the earliest date the city is mentioned in a document. The document was signed in
      <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">
       Augsburg
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      By that time the
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Welf" title="House of Welf">
       Guelph
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">
       Henry the Lion
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Saxony" title="Duchy of Saxony">
       Duke of Saxony
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Bavaria" title="List of rulers of Bavaria">
       Bavaria
      </a>
      , had built a bridge over the river Isar next to a settlement of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedictine" title="Benedictine">
       Benedictine
      </a>
      monksthis was on the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Salt_Route" title="Old Salt Route">
       Old Salt Route
      </a>
      and a toll bridge.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1175, Munich was officially granted city status and received fortification. In 1180, with the trial of Henry the Lion,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Otto_I_of_Wittelsbach,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Otto I of Wittelsbach, Duke of Bavaria">
       Otto I Wittelsbach
      </a>
      became Duke of Bavaria and Munich was handed over to the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Munich_and_Freising" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Munich and Freising">
       Bishop of Freising
      </a>
      . (Wittelsbach's heirs, the
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Wittelsbach" title="House of Wittelsbach">
       Wittelsbach dynasty
      </a>
      , would rule Bavaria until 1918.) In 1240, Munich was transferred to
      <a href="/wiki/Otto_II_Wittelsbach,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Otto II Wittelsbach, Duke of Bavaria">
       Otto II Wittelsbach
      </a>
      and in 1255, when the
      <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Bavaria" title="Duchy of Bavaria">
       Duchy of Bavaria
      </a>
      was split in two, Munich became the ducal residence of
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">
       Upper Bavaria
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Duke
      <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Louis IV, Holy Roman Emperor">
       Louis IV
      </a>
      , a native of Munich, was elected German king in 1314 and crowned as
      <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">
       Holy Roman Emperor
      </a>
      in 1328. He strengthened the city's position by granting it the salt monopoly, thus assuring it of additional income. In the late 15th century Munich underwent a revival of
      <a href="/wiki/Gothic_art" title="Gothic art">
       gothic arts
      </a>
      the Old Town Hall was enlarged, and Munich's largest
      <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">
       gothic
      </a>
      church, now a cathedralthe
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Frauenkirche" title="Munich Frauenkirche">
       Frauenkirche
      </a>
      constructed in only twenty years, starting in 1468.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_of_reunited_Bavaria">
       Capital of reunited Bavaria
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Capital of reunited Bavaria">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marcktzumuenchen.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="579" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marcktzumuenchen.png/220px-Marcktzumuenchen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marcktzumuenchen.png/330px-Marcktzumuenchen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marcktzumuenchen.png/440px-Marcktzumuenchen.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marcktzumuenchen.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Marienplatz" title="Marienplatz">
         Marienplatz
        </a>
        , Munich about 1650
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="560" data-file-width="378" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg/170px-Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg/255px-Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg/340px-Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mun_flags_frauenkirche.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Banners with the colours of Munich (left) and Bavaria (right) with the
        <a href="/wiki/Munich_Frauenkirche" title="Munich Frauenkirche">
         Frauenkirche
        </a>
        in the background
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      When Bavaria was reunited in 1506, Munich became its capital. The arts and politics became increasingly influenced by the court (see
      <a href="/wiki/Orlande_de_Lassus" title="Orlande de Lassus">
       Orlando di Lasso
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Sch%C3%BCtz" title="Heinrich Schtz">
       Heinrich Schuetz
      </a>
      and later
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">
       Mozart
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">
       Richard Wagner
      </a>
      ). During the 16th century Munich was a centre of the German
      <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">
       counter reformation
      </a>
      , and also of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
       renaissance
      </a>
      arts. Duke
      <a href="/wiki/William_V,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="William V, Duke of Bavaria">
       Wilhelm V
      </a>
      commissioned the Jesuit
      <a href="/wiki/St._Michael%27s_Church,_Munich" title="St. Michael's Church, Munich">
       Michaelskirche
      </a>
      , which became a centre for the counter-reformation, and also built the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofbr%C3%A4uhaus" title="Hofbruhaus">
       Hofbruhaus
      </a>
      for brewing brown beer in 1589. The
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_League_(German)" title="Catholic League (German)">
       Catholic League
      </a>
      was founded in Munich in 1609. In 1623 during the
      <a href="/wiki/Thirty_Years%27_War" title="Thirty Years' War">
       Thirty Years' War
      </a>
      Munich became electoral residence when
      <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Elector_of_Bavaria" title="Maximilian I, Elector of Bavaria">
       Maximilian I, Duke of Bavaria
      </a>
      was invested with the
      <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">
       electoral dignity
      </a>
      but in 1632 the city was occupied by
      <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus_of_Sweden" title="Gustavus Adolphus of Sweden">
       Gustav II Adolph of Sweden
      </a>
      . When the
      <a href="/wiki/Bubonic_plague" title="Bubonic plague">
       bubonic plague
      </a>
      broke out in 1634 and 1635 about one third of the population died. Under the regency of the Bavarian electors Munich was an important centre of baroque life but also had to suffer under
      <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">
       Habsburg
      </a>
      occupations in 1704 and 1742.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1806, the city became the capital of the new
      <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Bavaria" title="Kingdom of Bavaria">
       Kingdom of Bavaria
      </a>
      , with the state's parliament (the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Landtag" title="Landtag">
        Landtag
       </a>
       )
      </i>
      and the new
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Munich_and_Freising" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Munich and Freising">
       archdiocese of Munich and Freising
      </a>
      being located in the city. Twenty years later
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Maximilian_University_of_Munich" title="Ludwig Maximilian University of Munich">
       Landshut University
      </a>
      was moved to Munich. Many of the city's finest buildings belong to this period and were built under the first three Bavarian kings. Especially
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_I_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig I of Bavaria">
       Ludwig I
      </a>
      has rendered outstanding services to Munich's status as a centre of the arts, attracting numerous artists and enhancing the city's architectural substance with grand boulevards and buildings. On the other hand,
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_II_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig II of Bavaria">
       Ludwig II
      </a>
      , famous the world over as the fairytale king, held himself mostly aloof from his capital and focused more on his fanciful castles in the Bavarian countryside. Nevertheless, his patronage of Richard Wagner secured his posthumous reputation, as do his castles, which generate significant tourist income for Bavaria to this day. Later Prince Regent
      <a href="/wiki/Luitpold,_Prince_Regent_of_Bavaria" title="Luitpold, Prince Regent of Bavaria">
       Luitpold's
      </a>
      years as regent were marked by tremendous artistic and cultural activity in Munich, enhancing its status as a cultural force of global importance (see
      <a href="/wiki/Franz_Stuck" title="Franz Stuck">
       Franz von Stuck
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Der_Blaue_Reiter" title="Der Blaue Reiter">
       Der Blaue Reiter
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I_to_World_War_II">
       World War I to World War II
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: World War I to World War II">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Following the outbreak of World War I in 1914, life in Munich became very difficult, as the Allied blockade of Germany led to food and fuel shortages. During French air raids in 1916, three bombs fell on Munich. After World War I, the city was at the centre of much political unrest. In November 1918 on the eve of revolution,
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_III_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig III of Bavaria">
       Ludwig III
      </a>
      and his family fled the city. After the murder of the first republican
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_Ministers-President_of_Bavaria" title="List of Ministers-President of Bavaria">
       premier of Bavaria
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Eisner" title="Kurt Eisner">
       Kurt Eisner
      </a>
      in February 1919 by
      <a href="/wiki/Anton_Graf_von_Arco_auf_Valley" title="Anton Graf von Arco auf Valley">
       Anton Graf von Arco auf Valley
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bavarian_Soviet_Republic" title="Bavarian Soviet Republic">
       Bavarian Soviet Republic
      </a>
      was proclaimed. When Communists had taken power,
      <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">
       Lenin
      </a>
      , who had lived in Munich some years before, sent a congratulatory telegram, but the Soviet Republic was put down on 3 May 1919 by the
      <a href="/wiki/Freikorps" title="Freikorps">
       Freikorps
      </a>
      . While the republican government had been restored, Munich subsequently became a hotbed of extremist politics, among which
      <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
       Adolf Hitler
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">
       National Socialism
      </a>
      rose to prominence.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wardamage2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="617" data-file-width="800" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wardamage2.jpg/220px-Wardamage2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wardamage2.jpg/330px-Wardamage2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Wardamage2.jpg/440px-Wardamage2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wardamage2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Bombing damage to the Altstadt. Note the roofless and pockmarked Altes Rathaus looking up the Tal. The roofless Heilig-Geist-Kirche is on the right of the photo. Its spire, without the copper top, is behind the church. The Talbruck gate tower is missing completely.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 1923 Hitler and his supporters, who were then concentrated in Munich, staged the
      <a href="/wiki/Beer_Hall_Putsch" title="Beer Hall Putsch">
       Beer Hall Putsch
      </a>
      , an attempt to overthrow the
      <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">
       Weimar Republic
      </a>
      and seize power. The revolt failed, resulting in Hitler's arrest and the temporary crippling of the
      <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">
       Nazi Party
      </a>
      , which was virtually unknown outside Munich. The city once again became a Nazi stronghold when the National Socialists took power in Germany in 1933. The National Socialist Workers Party created their first
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nazi_concentration_camp" title="Nazi concentration camp">
       concentration camp
      </a>
      at
      <a href="/wiki/Dachau_concentration_camp" title="Dachau concentration camp">
       Dachau
      </a>
      , 10 miles (16 kilometres) north-west of the city. Because of its importance to the rise of National Socialism, Munich was referred to as the
      <i>
       Hauptstadt der Bewegung
      </i>
      ("Capital of the Movement"). The
      <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">
       NSDAP
      </a>
      headquarters was in Munich and many
      <i>
       Fhrerbauten
      </i>
      ("
      <i>
       Fhrer
      </i>
      -buildings") were built around the
      <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsplatz,_Munich" title="Knigsplatz, Munich">
       Knigsplatz
      </a>
      , some of which have survived to this day.
     </p>
     <p>
      The city is known as the site of the culmination of the policy of
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">
       appeasement
      </a>
      employed by Britain and France leading up to World War II. It was in Munich that British Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Neville_Chamberlain" title="Neville Chamberlain">
       Neville Chamberlain
      </a>
      assented to the annexation of Czechoslovakia's Sudetenland region into Greater Germany in the hopes of sating the desires of Hitler's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_Reich" title="Third Reich">
       Third Reich
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Munich was the base of the
      <a href="/wiki/White_Rose" title="White Rose">
       White Rose
      </a>
      , a student
      <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">
       resistance movement
      </a>
      from June 1942 to February 1943. The core members were arrested and executed following a distribution of leaflets in
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Maximilian_University_of_Munich" title="Ludwig Maximilian University of Munich">
       Munich University
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/White_Rose" title="White Rose">
       Hans and Sophie Scholl
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The city was heavily damaged by allied bombing during World War II  the city was hit by 71 air raids over a period of five years.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Postwar">
       Postwar
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Postwar">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BMW_Welt_Night.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1700" data-file-width="3000" height="125" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/BMW_Welt_Night.jpg/220px-BMW_Welt_Night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/BMW_Welt_Night.jpg/330px-BMW_Welt_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/BMW_Welt_Night.jpg/440px-BMW_Welt_Night.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BMW_Welt_Night.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/BMW_Welt" title="BMW Welt">
         BMW Welt
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After US occupation in 1945, Munich was completely rebuilt following a meticulous and  by comparison to other war-ravaged
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_German" title="West German">
       West German
      </a>
      cities
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
       rather conservative plan which preserved its pre-war street grid. In 1957 Munich's population passed the 1 million mark. The city continued to play a highly significant role in matters of German economy, politics and culture, giving rise to its nickname
      <i>
       Heimliche Hauptstadt
      </i>
      ("secret capital") in the decades after World War II.
     </p>
     <p>
      Munich was the site of the
      <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">
       1972 Summer Olympics
      </a>
      , during which
      <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">
       Israeli
      </a>
      athletes were assassinated by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palestinian_Fedayeen" title="Palestinian Fedayeen">
       Palestinian fedayeen
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_massacre" title="Munich massacre">
       Munich massacre
      </a>
      , when gunmen from the Palestinian "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Black_September_(group)" title="Black September (group)">
       Black September
      </a>
      " group took hostage members of the Israeli Olympic team.
     </p>
     <p>
      Most Munich residents enjoy a high quality of life. Mercer HR Consulting consistently rates the city among the top 10 cities with the highest quality of life worldwide  a 2011 survey ranked Munich as 4th.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The same company also ranks Munich as the world's 39th most expensive city to live in and the most expensive major city in Germany.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Munich enjoys a thriving economy, driven by the information technology, biotechnology, and publishing sectors. Environmental pollution is low, although as of 2006 the city council is concerned about levels of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particulate_matter" title="Particulate matter">
       particulate matter
      </a>
      (PM), especially along the city's major thoroughfares. Since the enactment of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Particulate#EU_legislation" title="Particulate">
       EU legislation concerning the concentration of particulate
      </a>
      in the air, environmental groups such as
      <a href="/wiki/Greenpeace" title="Greenpeace">
       Greenpeace
      </a>
      have staged large protest rallies to urge the city council and the State government to take a harder stance on pollution.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Today, the crime rate is low compared with other large German cities, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">
       Hamburg
      </a>
      or Berlin. For its high quality of life and safety the city has been nicknamed "Toytown"
      <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.toytowngermany.com" rel="nofollow">
       [3]
      </a>
      among the English-speaking residents. German inhabitants call it "Millionendorf", an expression which means "village of a million people".
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
       Geography
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Geography">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3285" data-file-width="4861" height="149" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/220px-Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/330px-Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/440px-Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Stadtbild_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The inner city (2013).
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1467" data-file-width="3072" height="105" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG/220px-Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG/330px-Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG/440px-Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Englischer_Garten_from_Monopteros.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Munich: View from the
        <a href="/wiki/Englischer_Garten" title="Englischer Garten">
         Englischer Garten
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich lies on the elevated plains of
      <a href="/wiki/Upper_Bavaria" title="Upper Bavaria">
       Upper Bavaria
      </a>
      , about 50km (31.07mi) north of the northern edge of the
      <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">
       Alps
      </a>
      , at an altitude of about 520m (1,706.04ft)
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" title="Above mean sea level">
       ASL
      </a>
      . The local rivers are the
      <a href="/wiki/Isar" title="Isar">
       Isar
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrm" title="Wrm">
       Wrm
      </a>
      . Munich is situated in the Northern
      <a href="/wiki/Foothills" title="Foothills">
       Alpine Foreland
      </a>
      . The northern part of this sandy plateau includes a highly fertile
      <a href="/wiki/Flint" title="Flint">
       flint
      </a>
      area which is no longer affected by the
      <a href="/wiki/Fold_(geology)" title="Fold (geology)">
       folding
      </a>
      processes found in the Alps, while the southern part is covered with
      <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">
       morainic
      </a>
      hills. Between these are fields of
      <a href="/wiki/Fluvio-glacial" title="Fluvio-glacial">
       fluvio-glacial
      </a>
      out-wash, such as around Munich. Wherever these deposits get thinner, the
      <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">
       ground water
      </a>
      can permeate the gravel surface and flood the area, leading to
      <a href="/wiki/Marsh" title="Marsh">
       marshes
      </a>
      as in the north of Munich.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">
       Climate
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Munich's climate is classified in the
      <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Kppen climate classification">
       Kppen classification
      </a>
      as Cfb (
      <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">
       Oceanic
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      The warmest month of the year, on average, is July. The coolest month of the year, on average, is January.
     </p>
     <p>
      Showers and thunderstorms bring the highest average monthly precipitation totals in late spring and throughout the summer. June, on average, records the most precipitation of any month. The winter months tend to bring lower precipitation, on average, and February averages the least amount of monthly precipitation for the year.
     </p>
     <p>
      The higher elevation of Munich and the proximity of the Alps play a significant role on the climate, causing the city to have more rain and snow than many other parts of Germany. The Alps affect the city's climate in other ways too: the warm downhill wind from the Alps (fhn wind), which can raise temperatures sharply within a few hours even in the winter is but one example.
     </p>
     <p>
      Being at the center of Europe, Munich is subject to many climatic influences, so that weather conditions there are more variable than in other European towns, especially those further west and south of the Alps
     </p>
     <p>
      At Munich's official weather station, the highest and lowest temperatures ever measured are 37.1C, on 13 August 2003, and -31.6C, on 12 February 1929.
     </p>

     <p>
      In July 2007, Munich had 1.34million inhabitants; 300,129 of those did not hold
      <a href="/wiki/German_nationality_law" title="German nationality law">
       German citizenship
      </a>
      . The city has strong
      <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">
       Turkish
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
       Balkan
      </a>
      communities. The largest groups of foreign nationals were
      <a href="/wiki/Turkish_people" title="Turkish people">
       Turks
      </a>
      (43,309),
      <a href="/wiki/Albanians" title="Albanians">
       Albanians
      </a>
      (30,385),
      <a href="/wiki/Croats" title="Croats">
       Croats
      </a>
      (24,866),
      <a href="/wiki/Serbs" title="Serbs">
       Serbs
      </a>
      (24,439),
      <a href="/wiki/Greeks" title="Greeks">
       Greeks
      </a>
      (22,486),
      <a href="/wiki/Austrians" title="Austrians">
       Austrians
      </a>
      (21,411), and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">
       Italians
      </a>
      (20,847). 37% of foreign nationals come from the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      From only 24,000 inhabitants in 1700, the population doubled about every 30 years. For example, it had 100,000 people in 1852 and then 250,000 people in 1883; by 1901, the figure had doubled again to 500,000. Since then, Munich has become Germany's third largest city. In 1933, 840,901 inhabitants were counted and in 1957, Munich's population passed the 1 million mark.
     </p>
     <p>
      About 40% of Munich's residents are not affiliated with any religious group, and this ratio represents the fastest growing segment of the population. As in the rest of Germany, the Roman Catholic and Protestant churches have experienced a continuous, slow decline in their memberships. As of 31 December 2013, 34.7% of the city's inhabitants were
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
       Roman Catholic
      </a>
      , 12.5%
      <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
       Protestant
      </a>
      , and 0.3%
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
       Jewish
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      About 3% adhere to other Christian denominations and 7% are Muslim. There is also a small Old Catholic parish and an English-speaking parish of the
      <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">
       Episcopal Church
      </a>
      in the city.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">
       Politics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Politics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Munich's current mayor is
      <a href="/wiki/Dieter_Reiter" title="Dieter Reiter">
       Dieter Reiter
      </a>
      of the
      <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">
       Social Democratic Party of Germany
      </a>
      . Munich has been governed by the SPD for all but six years since 1948. This is remarkable because Bavariaand particularly southern Bavariahas long been a conservative stronghold, with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_Social_Union_of_Bavaria" title="Christian Social Union of Bavaria">
       Christian Social Union
      </a>
      winning
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_majority" title="Absolute majority">
       absolute majorities
      </a>
      among the Bavarian electorate in many elections at the communal, state, and federal levels, and leading the Bavarian state government for all but three years since 1946. Bavaria's second most populous city,
      <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">
       Nuremberg
      </a>
      , is also one of the very few Bavarian cities governed by a SPD-led coalition.
     </p>
     <p>
      As the capital of the Free State of Bavaria, Munich is an important political centre in Germany and the seat of the
      <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_Bavaria" title="Landtag of Bavaria">
       Bavarian State Parliament
      </a>
      , the Staatskanzlei (the State Chancellery) and of all state departments.
     </p>
     <p>
      Several national and international authorities are located in Munich, including the
      <a href="/wiki/Federal_Finance_Court_of_Germany" title="Federal Finance Court of Germany">
       Federal Finance Court of Germany
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Patent_Office" title="European Patent Office">
       European Patent Office
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Subdivisions">
       Subdivisions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Subdivisions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Munich" title="Boroughs of Munich">
       Boroughs of Munich
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Since the administrative reform in 1992, Munich is divided into 25
      <a href="/wiki/Borough" title="Borough">
       boroughs
      </a>
      or
      <i>
       Stadtbezirke
      </i>
      , which themselves consist of sometimes quite distinct smaller quarters.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">

       </a>
