     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">
       Architecture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Architecture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Munich" title="Architecture of Munich">
       Architecture of Munich
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1800" data-file-width="2089" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg/220px-Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg/330px-Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg/440px-Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rathaus_and_Marienplatz_from_Peterskirche_-_August_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The New Town Hall and
        <a href="/wiki/Marienplatz" title="Marienplatz">
         Marienplatz
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2464" data-file-width="3952" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg/220px-Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg/330px-Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg/440px-Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Frauenkirche_Munich_-_View_from_Peterskirche_Tower2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Munich_Frauenkirche" title="Munich Frauenkirche">
         Frauenkirche
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BCnchen,_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3302" data-file-width="4403" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg/220px-M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg/330px-M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg/440px-M%C3%BCnchen%2C_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BCnchen,_Viktualienmarkt_met_das_Alte_Rathaus_D-1-62-000-4289_positie2_2012-08-05_15.29.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Viktualienmarkt with the Alten Rathaus
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The city is an eclectic mix of historic buildings and modern architecture, Munich having reconstructed the ruins of those historic buildings that have been destroyed in World War II while creating new landmarks of architecture. A survey, conducted by the Society's Center for Sustainable Destinations for the
      <a href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Traveler" title="National Geographic Traveler">
       National Geographic Traveler
      </a>
      , chose over 100 historic places around the world and ranked Munich as the 30th best destination.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Inner_city">
       Inner city
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Inner city">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      At the centre of the city is the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Marienplatz" title="Marienplatz">
        Marienplatz
       </a>
      </i>
      a large open square named after the Mariensule, a
      <a href="/wiki/Marian_and_Holy_Trinity_columns" title="Marian and Holy Trinity columns">
       Marian column
      </a>
      in its centrewith the
      <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Hall,_Munich" title="Old Town Hall, Munich">
       Old
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Town_Hall,_Munich" title="New Town Hall, Munich">
       New Town Hall
      </a>
      . Its tower contains the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Rathaus-Glockenspiel" title="Rathaus-Glockenspiel">
        Rathaus-Glockenspiel
       </a>
      </i>
      . Three gates of the demolished medieval fortification have survived to this daythe
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Isartor" title="Isartor">
        Isartor
       </a>
      </i>
      in the east, the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sendlinger_Tor" title="Sendlinger Tor">
        Sendlinger Tor
       </a>
      </i>
      in the south and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Karlstor" title="Karlstor">
        Karlstor
       </a>
      </i>
      in the west of the inner city. The Karlstor leads up to the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Karlsplatz_(Stachus)" title="Karlsplatz (Stachus)">
        Stachus
       </a>
      </i>
      , a grand square dominated by the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Justizpalast_(Munich)" title="Justizpalast (Munich)">
        Justizpalast
       </a>
       (Palace of Justice)
      </i>
      and a fountain.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Church,_Munich" title="St. Peter's Church, Munich">
        Peterskirche
       </a>
      </i>
      close to Marienplatz is the oldest church of the inner city. It was first built during the
      <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">
       Romanesque
      </a>
      period, and was the focus of the early monastic settlement in Munich before the city's official foundation in 1158. Nearby St. Peter the Gothic hall-church
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Heiliggeistkirche_(Munich)" title="Heiliggeistkirche (Munich)">
        Heiliggeistkirche
       </a>
      </i>
      (The Church of the Holy Spirit) was converted to baroque style from 1724 onwards and looks down upon the
      <a href="/wiki/Viktualienmarkt" title="Viktualienmarkt">
       Viktualienmarkt
      </a>
      , the most popular market of Munich.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Frauenkirche" title="Munich Frauenkirche">
        Frauenkirche
       </a>
      </i>
      is the most famous building in the city centre and serves as the cathedral for the
      <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Munich_and_Freising" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Munich and Freising">
       Archdiocese of Munich and Freising
      </a>
      . The nearby
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/St._Michael%27s_Church,_Munich" title="St. Michael's Church, Munich">
        Michaelskirche
       </a>
      </i>
      is the largest
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">
       renaissance
      </a>
      church north of the Alps, while the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Theatine_Church,_Munich" title="Theatine Church, Munich">
        Theatinerkirche
       </a>
      </i>
      is a
      <a href="/wiki/Basilica" title="Basilica">
       basilica
      </a>
      in Italianate high baroque which had a major influence on Southern German
      <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">
       baroque
      </a>
      architecture. Its dome dominates the
      <a href="/wiki/Odeonsplatz" title="Odeonsplatz">
       Odeonsplatz
      </a>
      . Other baroque churches in the inner city which are worth a detour are the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/B%C3%BCrgersaalkirche_(Munich)" title="Brgersaalkirche (Munich)">
        Brgersaalkirche
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Trinity_Church_(Munich)" title="Trinity Church (Munich)">
        Dreifaltigkeitskirche
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/St._Anna_Damenstiftskirche_(Munich)" title="St. Anna Damenstiftskirche (Munich)">
        St. Anna Damenstiftskirche
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Parish_Church_of_St._Anna_(Lehel,_Munich)" title="Parish Church of St. Anna (Lehel, Munich)">
        St. Anna im Lehel
       </a>
      </i>
      , the first
      <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">
       rococo
      </a>
      church in Bavaria. The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Asamkirche,_Munich" title="Asamkirche, Munich">
        Asamkirche
       </a>
      </i>
      was endowed and built by the Brothers
      <a href="/wiki/Cosmas_Damian_Asam" title="Cosmas Damian Asam">
       Asam
      </a>
      , pioneering artists of the rococo period.
     </p>
     <p>
      The large
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Residenz" title="Munich Residenz">
        Residenz
       </a>
      </i>
      palace complex (begun in 1385) on the edge of Munich's Old Town, Germany's largest urban palace, ranks among Europe's most significant museums of interior decoration. Having undergone several extensions, it contains also the
      <a href="/wiki/Schatzkammer" title="Schatzkammer">
       treasury
      </a>
      and the splendid rococo
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Cuvilli%C3%A9s_Theatre" title="Cuvillis Theatre">
        Cuvillis Theatre
       </a>
      </i>
      . Next door to the Residenz the neo-classical opera, the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_Munich" title="National Theatre Munich">
        National Theatre
       </a>
      </i>
      was erected. Among the baroque and neoclassical mansions which still exist in Munich are the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Palais_Porcia" title="Palais Porcia">
        Palais Porcia
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Palais_Preysing" title="Palais Preysing">
        Palais Preysing
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palais_Holnstein" title="Palais Holnstein">
        Palais Holnstein
       </a>
      </i>
      and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Prinz-Carl-Palais" title="Prinz-Carl-Palais">
        Prinz-Carl-Palais
       </a>
      </i>
      . All mansions are situated close to the Residenz, same as the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Alter_Hof" title="Alter Hof">
        Alte Hof
       </a>
      </i>
      , a medieval castle and first residence of the Wittelsbach dukes in Munich.
     </p>
     <p>
      Lehel, a bourgeoise quarter east of the Altstadt, is characterized by countless well-preserved (and in parts excellently reconstructed) town houses, giving a thorough impression of the "old Munich" outside of the main tourist routes.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/St._Luke%27s_Church,_Munich" title="St. Luke's Church, Munich">
        St. Lukas
       </a>
      </i>
      is the largest Protestant Church in Munich.
     </p>
     <p>
      The inner city has been recreated
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in the virtual world of
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Life" title="Second Life">
       Second Life
      </a>
      and can be visited for a virtual sight seeing tour.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_avenues_and_squares">
       Royal avenues and squares
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Royal avenues and squares">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg/220px-Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg/330px-Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg/440px-Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ludwigstra%C3%9FeMUC.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ludwigstra%C3%9Fe_(Munich)" title="Ludwigstrae (Munich)">
         Ludwigstrasse
        </a>
        from above,
        <a href="/wiki/Highlight_Towers" title="Highlight Towers">
         Highlight Towers
        </a>
        in the background
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Four grand royal avenues of the 19th century with magnificent official buildings connect Munich's inner city with its then-suburbs:
     </p>
     <p>
      The neoclassical
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Brienner_Stra%C3%9Fe_(Munich)" title="Brienner Strae (Munich)">
        Briennerstrasse
       </a>
      </i>
      , starting at
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Odeonsplatz" title="Odeonsplatz">
        Odeonsplatz
       </a>
      </i>
      on the northern fringe of the Old Town close to the Residenz, runs from east to west and opens into the impressive
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsplatz,_Munich" title="Knigsplatz, Munich">
        Knigsplatz
       </a>
      </i>
      , designed with the "
      <a href="/wiki/Doric_order" title="Doric order">
       Doric
      </a>
      "
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Propylaea_(Munich)" title="Propylaea (Munich)">
        Propylen
       </a>
      </i>
      , the "
      <a href="/wiki/Ionic_order" title="Ionic order">
       Ionic
      </a>
      "
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Glyptothek" title="Glyptothek">
        Glyptothek
       </a>
      </i>
      and the "
      <a href="/wiki/Corinthian_order" title="Corinthian order">
       Corinthian
      </a>
      "
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Staatliche_Antikensammlungen" title="Staatliche Antikensammlungen">
        State Museum of Classical Art
       </a>
      </i>
      , on its back side
      <a href="/wiki/St._Boniface%27s_Abbey,_Munich" title="St. Boniface's Abbey, Munich">
       St. Boniface's Abbey
      </a>
      was erected. The area around Knigsplatz is home to the
      <a href="/wiki/Kunstareal" title="Kunstareal">
       Kunstareal
      </a>
      , Munich's gallery and museum quarter (as described
      <a href="/wiki/Munich#Museums" title="Munich">
       below
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ludwigstra%C3%9Fe_(Munich)" title="Ludwigstrae (Munich)">
        Ludwigstrasse
       </a>
      </i>
      also begins at
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Odeonsplatz" title="Odeonsplatz">
        Odeonsplatz
       </a>
      </i>
      and runs from south to north, skirting the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Maximilian_University_of_Munich" title="Ludwig Maximilian University of Munich">
        Ludwig-Maximilians-Universitt
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ludwigskirche_(Munich)" title="Ludwigskirche (Munich)">
        St. Louis church
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_State_Library" title="Bavarian State Library">
        Bavarian State Library
       </a>
      </i>
      and numerous state ministries and palaces. The southern part of the avenue was constructed in Italian renaissance style, while the north is strongly influenced by Italian Romanesque architecture. The
      <a href="/wiki/Siegestor" title="Siegestor">
       Siegestor
      </a>
      (gate of victory) sits at the northern end of Ludwigstrae, where the latter passes over into Leopoldstrae and the district of
      <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">
       Schwabing
      </a>
      begins.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="1021" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg/220px-The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg/330px-The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg/440px-The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Maximilianeum_Building.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Maximilianeum" title="Maximilianeum">
         Maximilianeum
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The neo-Gothic
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Maximilianstra%C3%9Fe_(Munich)" title="Maximilianstrae (Munich)">
        Maximilianstrae
       </a>
      </i>
      starts at
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Max-Joseph-Platz" title="Max-Joseph-Platz">
        Max-Joseph-Platz
       </a>
      </i>
      , where the
      <i>
       Residenz
      </i>
      and the National Theatre are situated, and runs from west to east. The avenue is framed by elaborately structured neo-Gothic buildings which house, among others, the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Kammerspiele" title="Munich Kammerspiele">
        Schauspielhaus
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       Building of the district government of Upper Bavaria
      </i>
      and the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_Museum_of_Ethnology" title="State Museum of Ethnology">
        Museum of Ethnology
       </a>
      </i>
      . After crossing the river Isar, the avenue circles the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Maximilianeum" title="Maximilianeum">
        Maximilianeum
       </a>
      </i>
      , home of the
      <a href="/wiki/Landtag_of_Bavaria" title="Landtag of Bavaria">
       state parliament
      </a>
      . The western portion of Maximilianstrae is known for its designer shops, luxury boutiques, jewellery stores, and one of Munich's foremost five-star hotels, the
      <i>
       Hotel Vier Jahreszeiten
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Prinzregentenstra%C3%9Fe_(Munich)" title="Prinzregentenstrae (Munich)">
        Prinzregentenstrasse
       </a>
      </i>
      runs parallel to Maximilianstrae and begins at
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Prinz-Carl-Palais" title="Prinz-Carl-Palais">
        Prinz-Carl-Palais
       </a>
      </i>
      . Many museums can be found along the avenue, such as the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Haus_der_Kunst" title="Haus der Kunst">
        Haus der Kunst
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_National_Museum" title="Bavarian National Museum">
        Bavarian National Museum
       </a>
      </i>
      and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Schackgalerie" title="Schackgalerie">
        Schackgalerie
       </a>
      </i>
      . The avenue crosses the Isar and circles the
      <i>
       Friedensengel monument
      </i>
      , then passing the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Villa_Stuck" title="Villa Stuck">
        Villa Stuck
       </a>
      </i>
      and Hitler's old apartment. The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Prinzregententheater" title="Prinzregententheater">
        Prinzregententheater
       </a>
      </i>
      is at Prinzregentenplatz further to the east.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_boroughs">
       Other boroughs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Other boroughs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In
      <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">
       Schwabing
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Maxvorstadt" title="Maxvorstadt">
       Maxvorstadt
      </a>
      , many beautiful streets with continuous rows of
      <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnderzeit" title="Grnderzeit">
       Grnderzeit
      </a>
      buildings can be found. Rows of elegant town houses and spectacular urban palais in many colours, often elaborately decorated with ornamental details on their facades, make up large parts of the areas west of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leopoldstra%C3%9Fe" title="Leopoldstrae">
       Leopoldstrae
      </a>
      (Schwabing's main shopping street), while in the eastern areas between Leopoldstrae and
      <a href="/wiki/Englischer_Garten" title="Englischer Garten">
       Englischer Garten
      </a>
      similar buildings alternate with almost rural-looking houses and whimsical mini-castles, often decorated with small towers. Numerous tiny alleys and shady lanes connect the larger streets and little plazas of the area, conveying the legendary artist's quarter's flair and atmosphere convincingly like it was at the turn of the 20th century. The wealthy district of
      <a href="/wiki/Bogenhausen" title="Bogenhausen">
       Bogenhausen
      </a>
      in the east of Munich is another little-known area (at least among tourists) rich in extravagant architecture, especially around Prinzregentenstrae. One of Bogenhausen's most beautiful buildings is
      <a href="/wiki/Villa_Stuck" title="Villa Stuck">
       Villa Stuck
      </a>
      , famed residence of painter
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Franz_von_Stuck" title="Franz von Stuck">
       Franz von Stuck
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Two large baroque palaces in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nymphenburg" title="Nymphenburg">
       Nymphenburg
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oberschleissheim" title="Oberschleissheim">
       Oberschleissheim
      </a>
      are reminders of Bavaria's royal past.
      <i>
       Schloss Nymphenburg
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Nymphenburg_Palace" title="Nymphenburg Palace">
        Nymphenburg Palace
       </a>
      </i>
      ), some 6km (4mi) north west of the city centre, is surrounded by an impressive park and is considered to be one of Europe's most beautiful royal residences. 2km (1mi) north west of Nymphenburg Palace is
      <i>
       Schloss Blutenburg
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Blutenburg_Castle" title="Blutenburg Castle">
        Blutenburg Castle
       </a>
      </i>
      ), an old ducal country seat with a late-Gothic palace church.
      <i>
       Schloss Frstenried
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BCrstenried_Palace" title="Frstenried Palace">
        Frstenried Palace
       </a>
      </i>
      ), a baroque palace of similar structure to Nymphenburg but of much smaller size, was erected around the same time in the south west of Munich. The second large baroque residence is
      <i>
       Schloss Schleissheim
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Schleissheim_Palace" title="Schleissheim Palace">
        Schleissheim Palace
       </a>
      </i>
      ), located in the suburb of
      <a href="/wiki/Oberschlei%C3%9Fheim" title="Oberschleiheim">
       Oberschleissheim
      </a>
      , a palace complex encompassing three separate residences:
      <i>
       Altes Schloss Schleissheim
      </i>
      (the old palace),
      <i>
       Neues Schloss Schleissheim
      </i>
      (the new palace) and
      <i>
       Schloss Lustheim
      </i>
      (Lustheim Palace). Most parts of the palace complex serve as museums and art galleries.
      <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Museum" title="Deutsches Museum">
       Deutsches Museum
      </a>
      's
      <i>
       Flugwerft Schleissheim
      </i>
      flight exhibition centre is located nearby, on the Schleissheim Special Landing Field. The
      <a href="/wiki/Bavaria_statue" title="Bavaria statue">
       Bavaria statue
      </a>
      before the neo-classical
      <a href="/wiki/Ruhmeshalle_(Munich)" title="Ruhmeshalle (Munich)">
       Ruhmeshalle
      </a>
      is a monumental, bronze sand-cast 19th-century statue at
      <a href="/wiki/Theresienwiese" title="Theresienwiese">
       Theresienwiese
      </a>
      . The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnwald_castle" title="Grnwald castle">
       Grnwald castle
      </a>
      is the only medieval castle in the Munich area which still exisists.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1796" data-file-width="4921" height="80" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg/220px-Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg/330px-Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg/440px-Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Image-Schloss_Nymphenburg_Munich_CC_edit3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Nymphenburg_Palace" title="Nymphenburg Palace">
         Nymphenburg Palace
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BMW-HQ.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="973" data-file-width="731" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/BMW-HQ.jpg/170px-BMW-HQ.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/BMW-HQ.jpg/255px-BMW-HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/BMW-HQ.jpg/340px-BMW-HQ.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BMW-HQ.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">
         BMW
        </a>
        Headquarters
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/St_Michael_in_Berg_am_Laim_(Munich)" title="St Michael in Berg am Laim (Munich)">
        St Michael in Berg am Laim
       </a>
      </i>
      might be the most remarkable church in the suburbs. Most of the boroughs have parish churches which originate from the Middle Ages like the most famous church of pilgrimage in Munich
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Church,_Ramersdorf" title="St. Mary's Church, Ramersdorf">
        St Mary in Ramersdorf
       </a>
      </i>
      . The oldest church within the city borders is
      <i>
       Heilig Kreuz
      </i>
      in Frttmaning next to the Allianz-Arena, known for its Romanesque fresco. Especially in its suburbs, Munich features a wide and diverse array of modern architecture, although strict culturally sensitive height limitations for buildings have limited the construction of skyscrapers to avoid a loss of views to the distant Bavarian Alps. Most high-rise buildings are clustered at the northern edge of Munich in the skyline, like the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Hypo-Haus" title="Hypo-Haus">
        Hypo-Haus
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabella_High-Rise_Building" title="Arabella High-Rise Building">
        Arabella High-Rise Building
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Highlight_Towers" title="Highlight Towers">
        Highlight Towers
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uptown_Munich" title="Uptown Munich">
        Uptown Munich
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Mnchner Tor
      </i>
      and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/BMW_Headquarters" title="BMW Headquarters">
        BMW Headquarters
       </a>
      </i>
      next to the Olympic Park. Several other high-rise buildings are located near the city centre and on the
      <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">
       Siemens
      </a>
      campus in southern Munich. A landmark of modern Munich is also the architecture of the sport stadiums (as described
      <a href="/wiki/Munich#Sports" title="Munich">
       below
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      In Fasangarten is the former
      <a href="/wiki/McGraw_Kaserne" title="McGraw Kaserne">
       McGraw Kaserne
      </a>
      , a former U.S. army base, near
      <a href="/wiki/Stadelheim_Prison" title="Stadelheim Prison">
       Stadelheim Prison
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Parks">
       Parks
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Parks">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1631" data-file-width="2175" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg/220px-M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg/330px-M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg/440px-M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BCnchen_Hofgartentempel.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Hofgarten with the dome of the state chancellery near the
        <a href="/wiki/Munich_Residenz" title="Munich Residenz">
         Residenz
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich is a green city with numerous parks. The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Englischer_Garten" title="Englischer Garten">
        Englischer Garten
       </a>
      </i>
      , close to the city centre and covering an area of 3.7km
      <sup>
       2
      </sup>
      (1.4sqmi) (larger than Central Park in New York), is one of the world's largest urban public parks, and contains a
      <a href="/wiki/Naturism" title="Naturism">
       nudist
      </a>
      area, jogging tracks and bridle-paths. It was designed and laid out by
      <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Thompson" title="Benjamin Thompson">
       Benjamin Thompson
      </a>
      , Count of Rumford, for both pleasure and as a work area for the city's vagrants and homeless. Nowadays it is entirely a park with multiple
      <a href="/wiki/Beer_garden" title="Beer garden">
       Biergartens
      </a>
      , the most well known at the
      <a href="/wiki/Englischer_Garten#Chinesischer_Turm" title="Englischer Garten">
       Chinese Pagoda
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Other large green spaces are the modern
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Olympiapark,_Munich" title="Olympiapark, Munich">
        Olympiapark
       </a>
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Westpark_(Munich)" title="Westpark (Munich)">
        Westpark
       </a>
      </i>
      , and the parks of
      <a href="/wiki/Nymphenburg_Palace" title="Nymphenburg Palace">
       Nymphenburg Palace
      </a>
      (with the
      <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_M%C3%BCnchen-Nymphenburg" title="Botanischer Garten Mnchen-Nymphenburg">
       Botanischer Garten Mnchen-Nymphenburg
      </a>
      to the north), and
      <a href="/wiki/Schleissheim_Palace" title="Schleissheim Palace">
       Schleissheim Palace
      </a>
      . The city's oldest park is the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Hofgarten_(Munich)" title="Hofgarten (Munich)">
        Hofgarten
       </a>
      </i>
      , near the Residenz, and dating back to the 16th century. Best known for the largest beergarden in the town is the former royal
      <i>
       Hirschgarten
      </i>
      , founded in 1780 for deer which still live there.
     </p>
     <p>
      The city's
      <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">
       zoo
      </a>
      is the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tierpark_Hellabrunn" title="Tierpark Hellabrunn">
        Tierpark Hellabrunn
       </a>
      </i>
      near the Flaucher Island in the Isar in the south of the city. Another notable park is Ostpark, located in Perlach-Ramersdorf area which houses the swimming area,
      <i>
       Michaelibad
      </i>
      , one of the largest in Munich.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
       Sports
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
