        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sports_in_Munich" title="Sports in Munich">
       Sports in Munich
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4434" data-file-width="4811" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg/220px-Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg/330px-Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg/440px-Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Allianz_Arena_zu_verschiedenen_Zeiten.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">
         Allianz Arena
        </a>
        , the home stadium of
        <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">
         Bayern Munich
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/TSV_1860_M%C3%BCnchen" title="TSV 1860 Mnchen">
         1860 Munich
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Football">
       Football
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Football">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Munich" title="Football in Munich">
       Football in Munich
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich is home to several professional
      <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
       football
      </a>
      teams including
      <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">
       Bayern Munich
      </a>
      , Germany's most successful club and a multiple
      <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">
       UEFA Champions League
      </a>
      winner. The Munich area currently has three clubs:
      <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">
       Bayern Munich
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TSV_1860_Munich" title="TSV 1860 Munich">
       1860 Munich
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/SpVgg_Unterhaching" title="SpVgg Unterhaching">
       SpVgg Unterhaching
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">
       Bundesliga
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/2._Bundesliga" title="2. Bundesliga">
       2. Bundesliga
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/3._Liga" title="3. Liga">
       3. Liga
      </a>
      respectively, which are the top three leagues in the
      <a href="/wiki/German_football_league_system" title="German football league system">
       German football league system
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball">
       Basketball
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Basketball">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich_(basketball)" title="FC Bayern Munich (basketball)">
       FC Bayern Munich Basketball
      </a>
      currently playing in Beko Basket Bundesliga.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hockey">
       Hockey
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hockey">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The city's ice hockey club is
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eishockeyclub_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Eishockeyclub Mnchen">
       EHC Munich
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">
       Olympics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Olympics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Munich_Olympiapark.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1276" data-file-width="4021" height="70" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Munich_Olympiapark.jpg/220px-Munich_Olympiapark.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Munich_Olympiapark.jpg/330px-Munich_Olympiapark.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Munich_Olympiapark.jpg/440px-Munich_Olympiapark.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Munich_Olympiapark.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Olympiasee in Olympiapark, Munich
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich has also hosted the
      <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">
       1972 Summer Olympics
      </a>
      and was one of the host cities for the
      <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">
       2006 Football World Cup
      </a>
      which was not held in Munich's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olympic_Stadium_(Munich)" title="Olympic Stadium (Munich)">
       Olympic Stadium
      </a>
      but in a new
      <a href="/wiki/Soccer-specific_stadium" title="Soccer-specific stadium">
       football specific stadium
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">
       Allianz Arena
      </a>
      . Munich bid to host the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2018_Winter_Olympic_Games" title="2018 Winter Olympic Games">
       2018 Winter Olympic Games
      </a>
      but lost to
      <a href="/wiki/Pyeongchang_County" title="Pyeongchang County">
       Pyeongchang
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In September 2011 the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DOSB" title="DOSB">
       DOSB
      </a>
      President
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Bach" title="Thomas Bach">
       Thomas Bach
      </a>
      confirmed that Munich would bid again for the Winter Olympics in the future.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
       <a href="#cite_note-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
       Culture
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Culture">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Language">
       Language
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Language">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Bavarian_language" title="Austro-Bavarian language">
       Austro-Bavarian language
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Bavarian_language" title="Austro-Bavarian language">
       Austro-Bavarian language
      </a>
      is spoken in and around Munich, with its variety
      <i>
       Upper Bavarian
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       Oberbayrisch
      </i>
      ). Austro-Bavarian has no official status by the Bavarian authorities or local government yet is recognised by the
      <a href="/wiki/SIL_International" title="SIL International">
       SIL
      </a>
      and has its own ISO-639 code.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">
       Museums
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Museums">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1366" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg/220px-Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg/330px-Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg/440px-Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bayerisches_Nationalmuseum_-_Muenchen_-_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_National_Museum" title="Bavarian National Museum">
         Bavarian National Museum
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Museum" title="Deutsches Museum">
        Deutsches Museum
       </a>
      </i>
      or German Museum, located on an island in the River Isar, is the largest and one of the oldest science museums in the world. Three redundant exhibition buildings which are under a protection order were converted to house the
      <i>
       Verkehrsmuseum
      </i>
      , which houses the land transport collections of the Deutsches Museum. Deutsches Museum's
      <i>
       Flugwerft Schleissheim
      </i>
      flight exhibition centre is located nearby, on the Schleissheim Special Landing Field.Several non-centralised museums (many of those are public collections at Ludwig-Maximilians-Universitt) show the expanded state collections of
      <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A4ontologisches_Museum_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Palontologisches Museum Mnchen">
       palaeontology
      </a>
      , geology,
      <a href="/wiki/Mineralogy" title="Mineralogy">
       mineralogy
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Zoologische_Staatssammlung_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Zoologische Staatssammlung Mnchen">
       zoology
      </a>
      , botany and anthropology.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/220px-Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/330px-Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg/440px-Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glyptothek_in_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Glyptothek" title="Glyptothek">
         Glyptothek
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The city has several important
      <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">
       art galleries
      </a>
      , most of which can be found in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kunstareal" title="Kunstareal">
        Kunstareal
       </a>
      </i>
      , including the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Alte_Pinakothek" title="Alte Pinakothek">
        Alte Pinakothek
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Neue_Pinakothek" title="Neue Pinakothek">
        Neue Pinakothek
       </a>
      </i>
      , the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pinakothek_der_Moderne" title="Pinakothek der Moderne">
        Pinakothek der Moderne
       </a>
      </i>
      and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_Brandhorst" title="Museum Brandhorst">
        Museum Brandhorst
       </a>
      </i>
      . Alte Pinakothek's monolithic structure contains a treasure trove of the works of European masters between the 14th and 18th centuries. The collection reflects the eclectic tastes of the Wittelsbachs over four centuries, and is sorted by schools over two sprawling floors. Major displays include
      <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_D%C3%BCrer" title="Albrecht Drer">
       Albrecht Drer
      </a>
      's Christ-like Self-Portrait, his Four Apostles,
      <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">
       Raphael's
      </a>
      paintings
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Canigiani_Holy_Family_(Raphael)" title="Canigiani Holy Family (Raphael)">
        The Canigiani Holy Family
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Tempi_Madonna_(Raphael)" title="Tempi Madonna (Raphael)">
        Madonna Tempi
       </a>
      </i>
      as well as
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Rubens" title="Peter Paul Rubens">
       Peter Paul Rubens
      </a>
      two-story-high
      <i>
       Judgment Day
      </i>
      . The gallery houses one of the world's most comprehensive Rubens collections. Before World War I, the
      <a href="/wiki/Der_Blaue_Reiter" title="Der Blaue Reiter">
       Blaue Reiter
      </a>
      group of artists worked in Munich. Many of their works can now be seen at the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Lenbachhaus" title="Lenbachhaus">
        Lenbachhaus
       </a>
      </i>
      . An important collection of Greek and Roman art is held in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Glyptothek" title="Glyptothek">
        Glyptothek
       </a>
      </i>
      and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Staatliche_Antikensammlungen" title="Staatliche Antikensammlungen">
        Staatliche Antikensammlung
       </a>
      </i>
      (State Antiquities Collection). King Ludwig I managed to acquire such famous pieces as the
      <a href="/wiki/Medusa_Rondanini" title="Medusa Rondanini">
       Medusa Rondanini
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Barberini_Faun" title="Barberini Faun">
       Barberini Faun
      </a>
      and figures from the
      <a href="/wiki/Temple_of_Aphaea" title="Temple of Aphaea">
       Temple of Aphaea
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Aegina" title="Aegina">
       Aegina
      </a>
      for the Glyptothek. Another important museum in the
      <a href="/wiki/Kunstareal" title="Kunstareal">
       Kunstareal
      </a>
      is the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Staatliche_Sammlung_f%C3%BCr_%C3%84gyptische_Kunst" title="Staatliche Sammlung fr gyptische Kunst">
        Egyptian Museum
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The famous gothic
      <a href="/wiki/Morris_dance" title="Morris dance">
       Morris dancers
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Grasser" title="Erasmus Grasser">
       Erasmus Grasser
      </a>
      are exhibited in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Stadtmuseum" title="Munich Stadtmuseum">
        Munich City Museum
       </a>
      </i>
      in the old gothic arsenal building in the inner city.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another area for the arts next to the Kunstareal is the
      <a href="/wiki/Altstadt-Lehel" title="Altstadt-Lehel">
       Lehel
      </a>
      quarter between the old town and the river Isar: The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Museum_Five_Continents" title="Museum Five Continents">
        Museum Five Continents
       </a>
      </i>
      in Maximilianstrae is the second largest collection in Germany of artifacts and objects from outside Europe, while the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_National_Museum" title="Bavarian National Museum">
        Bavarian National Museum
       </a>
      </i>
      and the adjoining
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_State_Archaeological_Collection" title="Bavarian State Archaeological Collection">
        Bavarian State Archaeological Collection
       </a>
      </i>
      in Prinzregentenstrasse rank among Europe's major art and cultural history museums. The nearby
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Schackgalerie" title="Schackgalerie">
        Schackgalerie
       </a>
      </i>
      is an important gallery of German 19th-century paintings.
     </p>
     <p>
      The former
      <a href="/wiki/Dachau_concentration_camp" title="Dachau concentration camp">
       Dachau concentration camp
      </a>
      is 16km (10mi) outside the city.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_literature">
       Arts and literature
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Arts and literature">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Munich is a major European cultural centre and has played host to many prominent composers including
      <a href="/wiki/Orlande_de_Lassus" title="Orlande de Lassus">
       Orlando di Lasso
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">
       W.A. Mozart
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Maria_von_Weber" title="Carl Maria von Weber">
       Carl Maria von Weber
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">
       Richard Wagner
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Mahler" title="Gustav Mahler">
       Gustav Mahler
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Strauss" title="Richard Strauss">
       Richard Strauss
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Max_Reger" title="Max Reger">
       Max Reger
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Orff" title="Carl Orff">
       Carl Orff
      </a>
      . With the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Biennale" title="Munich Biennale">
       Munich Biennale
      </a>
      founded by
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Werner_Henze" title="Hans Werner Henze">
       Hans Werner Henze
      </a>
      , and the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/A*Devantgarde" title="A*Devantgarde">
        A*DEvantgarde
       </a>
      </i>
      festival, the city still contributes to modern music theatre. Some of classical music's best-known pieces have been created in and around Munich by native composers, for example Richard Strauss's famous tone poem
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Also_sprach_Zarathustra_(Strauss)" title="Also sprach Zarathustra (Strauss)">
        Also sprach Zarathustra
       </a>
      </i>
      or Carl Orff's
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Carmina_Burana" title="Carmina Burana">
        Carmina Burana
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="722" data-file-width="1000" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg/220px-M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg/330px-M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg/440px-M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:M%C3%BCnchen_Nationaltheater_Interior.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_Munich" title="National Theatre Munich">
         National Theatre
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre_Munich" title="National Theatre Munich">
        Nationaltheater
       </a>
      </i>
      , where several of
      <a href="/wiki/Richard_Wagner" title="Richard Wagner">
       Richard Wagner's
      </a>
      operas had their premieres under the patronage of
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_II_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig II of Bavaria">
       Ludwig II of Bavaria
      </a>
      , is the home of the
      <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_State_Opera" title="Bavarian State Opera">
       Bavarian State Opera
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_State_Orchestra" title="Bavarian State Orchestra">
       Bavarian State Orchestra
      </a>
      . Next door, the modern
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Residenz_Theatre" title="Residenz Theatre">
        Residenz Theatre
       </a>
      </i>
      was erected in the building that had housed the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Cuvilli%C3%A9s_Theatre" title="Cuvillis Theatre">
        Cuvillis Theatre
       </a>
      </i>
      before World War II. Many operas were staged there, including the premiere of
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">
       Mozart's
      </a>
      <i>
       Idomeneo
      </i>
      in 1781. The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Staatstheater_am_G%C3%A4rtnerplatz" title="Staatstheater am Grtnerplatz">
        Grtnerplatz Theatre
       </a>
      </i>
      is a ballet and musical state theatre while another opera house, the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Prinzregententheater" title="Prinzregententheater">
        Prinzregententheater
       </a>
      </i>
      , has become the home of the Bavarian Theatre Academy. The modern
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gasteig" title="Gasteig">
        Gasteig
       </a>
      </i>
      centre houses the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Philharmonic" title="Munich Philharmonic">
       Munich Philharmonic Orchestra
      </a>
      . The third orchestra in Munich with international importance is the
      <a href="/wiki/Bavarian_Radio_Symphony_Orchestra" title="Bavarian Radio Symphony Orchestra">
       Bavarian Radio Symphony Orchestra
      </a>
      . Its primary concert venue is the
      <i>
       Herkulessaal
      </i>
      in the former city royal residence, the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Residenz" title="Munich Residenz">
       Munich Residenz
      </a>
      . Many important conductors have been attracted by the city's orchestras, including
      <a href="/wiki/Felix_Weingartner" title="Felix Weingartner">
       Felix Weingartner
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Pfitzner" title="Hans Pfitzner">
       Hans Pfitzner
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Rosbaud" title="Hans Rosbaud">
       Hans Rosbaud
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Knappertsbusch" title="Hans Knappertsbusch">
       Hans Knappertsbusch
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Sergiu_Celibidache" title="Sergiu Celibidache">
       Sergiu Celibidache
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/James_Levine" title="James Levine">
       James Levine
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_Thielemann" title="Christian Thielemann">
       Christian Thielemann
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lorin_Maazel" title="Lorin Maazel">
       Lorin Maazel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Kubel%C3%ADk" title="Rafael Kubelk">
       Rafael Kubelk
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Jochum" title="Eugen Jochum">
       Eugen Jochum
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sir_Colin_Davis" title="Sir Colin Davis">
       Sir Colin Davis
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Mariss_Jansons" title="Mariss Jansons">
       Mariss Jansons
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bruno_Walter" title="Bruno Walter">
       Bruno Walter
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Georg_Solti" title="Georg Solti">
       Georg Solti
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Zubin_Mehta" title="Zubin Mehta">
       Zubin Mehta
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Kent_Nagano" title="Kent Nagano">
       Kent Nagano
      </a>
      . A stage for shows, big events and musicals is the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Theater_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Deutsches Theater Mnchen">
        Deutsche Theater
       </a>
      </i>
      . It is Germany's largest theatre for guest performances.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FriedensengelMunchen.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/FriedensengelMunchen.JPG/220px-FriedensengelMunchen.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/FriedensengelMunchen.JPG/330px-FriedensengelMunchen.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f4/FriedensengelMunchen.JPG/440px-FriedensengelMunchen.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FriedensengelMunchen.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <i>
         Golden Friedensengel
        </i>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich's contributions to modern popular music are often overlooked in favour of its strong association with classical music, but they are numerous: The city has had a strong music scene in the 1960s and 1970s, with many internationally renowned bands and musicians frequently performing in its clubs. Furthermore, Munich was the centre of
      <a href="/wiki/Krautrock" title="Krautrock">
       Krautrock
      </a>
      in southern Germany, with many important bands such as
      <a href="/wiki/Amon_D%C3%BC%C3%BCl_II" title="Amon Dl II">
       Amon Dl II
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Embryo_(band)" title="Embryo (band)">
       Embryo
      </a>
      or
      <a href="/wiki/Popol_Vuh_(band)" title="Popol Vuh (band)">
       Popol Vuh
      </a>
      hailing from the city. In the 1970s, the
      <a href="/wiki/Musicland_Studios" title="Musicland Studios">
       Musicland Studios
      </a>
      developed into one of the most prominent recording studios in the world, with famous bands such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stones" title="Rolling Stones">
       Rolling Stones
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">
       Led Zeppelin
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Deep_Purple" title="Deep Purple">
       Deep Purple
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Queen_(band)" title="Queen (band)">
       Queen
      </a>
      recording albums there. Munich also played a significant role in the development of electronic music, with genre pioneer
      <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Moroder" title="Giorgio Moroder">
       Giorgio Moroder
      </a>
      , who invented
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synth" title="Synth">
       synth
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Disco" title="Disco">
       disco
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Electronic_dance_music" title="Electronic dance music">
       electronic dance music
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Donna_Summer" title="Donna Summer">
       Donna Summer
      </a>
      , one of disco music's most important performers, both living and working in the city. Other examples of notable musicians and bands from Munich are
      <a href="/wiki/Konstantin_Wecker" title="Konstantin Wecker">
       Konstantin Wecker
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="extiw" href="//de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Willy_Astor" title="de:Willy Astor">
       Willy Astor
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Spider_Murphy_Gang" title="Spider Murphy Gang">
       Spider Murphy Gang
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchener_Freiheit" title="Mnchener Freiheit">
       Mnchener Freiheit
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lou_Bega" title="Lou Bega">
       Lou Bega
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Megaherz" title="Megaherz">
       Megaherz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/FSK_(band)" title="FSK (band)">
       FSK
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Colour_Haze" title="Colour Haze">
       Colour Haze
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Sportfreunde_Stiller" title="Sportfreunde Stiller">
       Sportfreunde Stiller
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Next to the Bavarian Staatsschauspiel in the Residenz Theatre (Residenztheater), the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Kammerspiele" title="Munich Kammerspiele">
        Munich Kammerspiele
       </a>
      </i>
      in the Schauspielhaus is one of the most important German language theatres in the world. Since
      <a href="/wiki/Gotthold_Ephraim_Lessing" title="Gotthold Ephraim Lessing">
       Gotthold Ephraim Lessing
      </a>
      's premieres in 1775 many important writers have staged their plays in Munich such as
      <a href="/wiki/Christian_Friedrich_Hebbel" title="Christian Friedrich Hebbel">
       Christian Friedrich Hebbel
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Ibsen" title="Henrik Ibsen">
       Henrik Ibsen
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Hugo_von_Hofmannsthal" title="Hugo von Hofmannsthal">
       Hugo von Hofmannsthal
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The city is known as the second largest publishing center in the world (around 250 publishing houses have offices in the city), and many national and international publications are published in Munich, such as Arts in Munich, LAXMag and Prinz.
     </p>
     <p>
      At the turn of the 20th century, Munich, and especially its suburb of
      <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">
       Schwabing
      </a>
      , was the preeminent cultural metropolis of Germany. Its importance as a centre for both literature and the fine arts was second to none in Europe, with numerous German and non-German artists moving there. For example,
      <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">
       Wassily Kandinsky
      </a>
      chose Munich over Paris to study at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Akademie_der_Bildenden_K%C3%BCnste_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Akademie der Bildenden Knste Mnchen">
       Akademie der Bildenden Knste Mnchen
      </a>
      , and, along with many other painters and writers living in Schwabing at that time, had a profound influence on
      <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">
       modern art
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Prominent literary figures worked in Munich especially during the final decades of the Kingdom of Bavaria, the so-called
      <i>
       Prinzregentenzeit
      </i>
      (literally "prince regent's time") under the reign of
      <a href="/wiki/Luitpold,_Prince_Regent_of_Bavaria" title="Luitpold, Prince Regent of Bavaria">
       Luitpold, Prince Regent of Bavaria
      </a>
      , a period often described as a cultural Golden Age for both Munich and Bavaria as a whole. Among them were luminaries such as
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">
       Thomas Mann
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Mann" title="Heinrich Mann">
       Heinrich Mann
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paul_Johann_Ludwig_von_Heyse" title="Paul Johann Ludwig von Heyse">
       Paul Heyse
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rainer_Maria_Rilke" title="Rainer Maria Rilke">
       Rainer Maria Rilke
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Thoma" title="Ludwig Thoma">
       Ludwig Thoma
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fanny_zu_Reventlow" title="Fanny zu Reventlow">
       Fanny zu Reventlow
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Panizza" title="Oskar Panizza">
       Oskar Panizza
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Meyrink" title="Gustav Meyrink">
       Gustav Meyrink
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Max_Halbe" title="Max Halbe">
       Max Halbe
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Erich_M%C3%BChsam" title="Erich Mhsam">
       Erich Mhsam
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Frank_Wedekind" title="Frank Wedekind">
       Frank Wedekind
      </a>
      . For a short while, even
      <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">
       Vladimir Lenin
      </a>
      lived in Schwabing, where he wrote and published his most important work,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/What_Is_to_Be_Done%3F" title="What Is to Be Done?">
        What Is to Be Done?
       </a>
      </i>
      Central to Schwabing's bohemian scene (although they were actually often located in the nearby Maxvorstadt quarter) were
      <i>
       Knstlerlokale
      </i>
      (artist's cafs) like
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Caf%C3%A9_Stefanie" title="Caf Stefanie">
        Caf Stefanie
       </a>
      </i>
      or
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Simpl" title="Simpl">
        Simpl
       </a>
      </i>
      , whose liberal ways differed fundamentally from Munich's more traditional localities. The
      <i>
       Simpl
      </i>
      , which survives to this day (although with little relevance to the city's contemporary art scene), was named after Munich's famous anti-authoritarian satirical magazine
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Simplicissimus" title="Simplicissimus">
        Simplicissimus
       </a>
      </i>
      , founded in 1896 by
      <a href="/wiki/Albert_Langen" title="Albert Langen">
       Albert Langen
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Theodor_Heine" title="Thomas Theodor Heine">
       Thomas Theodor Heine
      </a>
      , which quickly became an important organ of the
      <i>
       Schwabinger Bohme
      </i>
      . Its strikingly modern caricatures and biting satirical attacks on
      <a href="/wiki/Wilhelminism" title="Wilhelminism">
       Wilhelmine
      </a>
      German society were the result of countless of collaborative efforts by many of the best visual artists and writers from Munich and elsewhere.
     </p>
     <p>
      The period immediately before World War I saw continued economic and cultural prominence for the city.
      <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Mann" title="Thomas Mann">
       Thomas Mann
      </a>
      wrote somewhat ironically in his novella
      <i>
       Gladius Dei
      </i>
      about this period: "Mnchen leuchtete" (literally "Munich shone"). Munich remained a centre of cultural life during the Weimar period, with figures such as
      <a href="/wiki/Lion_Feuchtwanger" title="Lion Feuchtwanger">
       Lion Feuchtwanger
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Bertolt_Brecht" title="Bertolt Brecht">
       Bertolt Brecht
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_Paul_Althaus" title="Peter Paul Althaus">
       Peter Paul Althaus
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stefan_George" title="Stefan George">
       Stefan George
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ricarda_Huch" title="Ricarda Huch">
       Ricarda Huch
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Ringelnatz" title="Joachim Ringelnatz">
       Joachim Ringelnatz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Oskar_Maria_Graf" title="Oskar Maria Graf">
       Oskar Maria Graf
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Annette_Kolb" title="Annette Kolb">
       Annette Kolb
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Toller" title="Ernst Toller">
       Ernst Toller
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Ball" title="Hugo Ball">
       Hugo Ball
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Mann" title="Klaus Mann">
       Klaus Mann
      </a>
      adding to the already established big names.
      <a href="/wiki/Karl_Valentin" title="Karl Valentin">
       Karl Valentin
      </a>
      was Germany's most important cabaret performer and comedian and is to this day well-remembered and beloved as a
      <a href="/wiki/Cultural_icon" title="Cultural icon">
       cultural icon
      </a>
      of his hometown. Between 1910 and 1940, he wrote and performed in many absurdist sketches and short films that were highly influential, earning him the nickname of "Charlie Chaplin of Germany". Many of Valentin's works wouldn't be imaginable without his congenial female partner
      <a href="/wiki/Liesl_Karlstadt" title="Liesl Karlstadt">
       Liesl Karlstadt
      </a>
      , who often played male characters to hilarious effect in their sketches. After World War II, Munich soon again became a focal point of the German literary scene and remains so to this day, with writers as diverse as
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Koeppen" title="Wolfgang Koeppen">
       Wolfgang Koeppen
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Erich_K%C3%A4stner" title="Erich Kstner">
       Erich Kstner
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Roth" title="Eugen Roth">
       Eugen Roth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Andersch" title="Alfred Andersch">
       Alfred Andersch
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Elfriede_Jelinek" title="Elfriede Jelinek">
       Elfriede Jelinek
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Magnus_Enzensberger" title="Hans Magnus Enzensberger">
       Hans Magnus Enzensberger
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ende" title="Michael Ende">
       Michael Ende
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Franz_Xaver_Kroetz" title="Franz Xaver Kroetz">
       Franz Xaver Kroetz
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Polt" title="Gerhard Polt">
       Gerhard Polt
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Patrick_S%C3%BCskind" title="Patrick Sskind">
       Patrick Sskind
      </a>
      calling the city their home.
     </p>
     <p>
      From the Gothic to the Baroque era, the fine arts were represented in Munich by artists like
      <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Grasser" title="Erasmus Grasser">
       Erasmus Grasser
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jan_Polack" title="Jan Polack">
       Jan Polack
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Johann_Baptist_Straub" title="Johann Baptist Straub">
       Johann Baptist Straub
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ignaz_G%C3%BCnther" title="Ignaz Gnther">
       Ignaz Gnther
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Hans_Krumpper" title="Hans Krumpper">
       Hans Krumpper
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Michael_Schwanthaler" title="Ludwig Michael Schwanthaler">
       Ludwig von Schwanthaler
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Cosmas_Damian_Asam" title="Cosmas Damian Asam">
       Cosmas Damian Asam
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Egid_Quirin_Asam" title="Egid Quirin Asam">
       Egid Quirin Asam
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Johann_Baptist_Zimmermann" title="Johann Baptist Zimmermann">
       Johann Baptist Zimmermann
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Johann_Michael_Fischer" title="Johann Michael Fischer">
       Johann Michael Fischer
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Cuvilli%C3%A9s" title="Franois de Cuvillis">
       Franois de Cuvillis
      </a>
      . Munich had already become an important place for painters like
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Rottmann" title="Carl Rottmann">
       Carl Rottmann
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Lovis_Corinth" title="Lovis Corinth">
       Lovis Corinth
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_von_Kaulbach" title="Wilhelm von Kaulbach">
       Wilhelm von Kaulbach
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Carl_Spitzweg" title="Carl Spitzweg">
       Carl Spitzweg
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Franz_von_Lenbach" title="Franz von Lenbach">
       Franz von Lenbach
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Franz_Stuck" title="Franz Stuck">
       Franz von Stuck
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karl_Piloty" title="Karl Piloty">
       Karl Piloty
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Leibl" title="Wilhelm Leibl">
       Wilhelm Leibl
      </a>
      when
      <a href="/wiki/Der_Blaue_Reiter" title="Der Blaue Reiter">
       Der Blaue Reiter
      </a>
      (The Blue Rider), a group of expressionist artists, was established in Munich in 1911. The city was home to the Blue Rider's painters
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Klee" title="Paul Klee">
       Paul Klee
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wassily_Kandinsky" title="Wassily Kandinsky">
       Wassily Kandinsky
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Alexej_von_Jawlensky" title="Alexej von Jawlensky">
       Alexej von Jawlensky
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Gabriele_M%C3%BCnter" title="Gabriele Mnter">
       Gabriele Mnter
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Franz_Marc" title="Franz Marc">
       Franz Marc
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/August_Macke" title="August Macke">
       August Macke
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Kubin" title="Alfred Kubin">
       Alfred Kubin
      </a>
      . Kandinsky's first abstract painting was created in Schwabing.
     </p>
     <p>
      Munich was (and in some cases, still is) home to many of the most important authors of the
      <a href="/wiki/New_German_Cinema" title="New German Cinema">
       New German Cinema
      </a>
      movement, including
      <a href="/wiki/Rainer_Werner_Fassbinder" title="Rainer Werner Fassbinder">
       Rainer Werner Fassbinder
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Werner_Herzog" title="Werner Herzog">
       Werner Herzog
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Reitz" title="Edgar Reitz">
       Edgar Reitz
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Achternbusch" title="Herbert Achternbusch">
       Herbert Achternbusch
      </a>
      . In 1971, the
      <a href="/wiki/Filmverlag_der_Autoren" title="Filmverlag der Autoren">
       Filmverlag der Autoren
      </a>
      was founded, cementing the city's role in the movement's history. Munich served as the location for many of Fassbinder's films, among them
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Ali:_Fear_Eats_the_Soul" title="Ali: Fear Eats the Soul">
        Ali: Fear Eats the Soul
       </a>
      </i>
      . The Hotel
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Deutsche_Eiche&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Deutsche Eiche (page does not exist)">
        Deutsche Eiche
       </a>
      </i>
      near Grtnerplatz was somewhat like a center of operations for Fassbinder and his "clan" of actors. New German Cinema is considered by far the most important artistic movement in German cinema history since the era of
      <a href="/wiki/German_Expressionism" title="German Expressionism">
       German Expressionism
      </a>
      in the 1920s.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1919, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bavaria_Film_Studios" title="Bavaria Film Studios">
       Bavaria Film Studios
      </a>
      were founded, which developed into one of Europe's biggest film studios. Famous directors like
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hitchcock" title="Alfred Hitchcock">
       Alfred Hitchcock
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Billy_Wilder" title="Billy Wilder">
       Billy Wilder
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Orson_Welles" title="Orson Welles">
       Orson Welles
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/John_Huston" title="John Huston">
       John Huston
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ingmar_Bergman" title="Ingmar Bergman">
       Ingmar Bergman
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">
       Stanley Kubrick
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Claude_Chabrol" title="Claude Chabrol">
       Claude Chabrol
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Umgelter" title="Fritz Umgelter">
       Fritz Umgelter
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Rainer_Werner_Fassbinder" title="Rainer Werner Fassbinder">
       Rainer Werner Fassbinder
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Petersen" title="Wolfgang Petersen">
       Wolfgang Petersen
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Wim_Wenders" title="Wim Wenders">
       Wim Wenders
      </a>
      made films there. Among the internationally well-known films produced at the studios are
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Pleasure_Garden_(film)" title="The Pleasure Garden (film)">
        The Pleasure Garden
       </a>
      </i>
      by Alfred Hitchcock,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Escape_(film)" title="The Great Escape (film)">
        The Great Escape
       </a>
      </i>
      by John Sturges,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Paths_of_Glory" title="Paths of Glory">
        Paths of Glory
       </a>
      </i>
      by Stanley Kubrick,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Willy_Wonka_%26_the_Chocolate_Factory" title="Willy Wonka &amp; the Chocolate Factory">
        Willy Wonka &amp; the Chocolate Factory
       </a>
      </i>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Mel_Stuart" title="Mel Stuart">
       Mel Stuart
      </a>
      and both
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Das_Boot" title="Das Boot">
        Das Boot
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Neverending_Story_(film)" title="The Neverending Story (film)">
        The Neverending Story
       </a>
      </i>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Petersen" title="Wolfgang Petersen">
       Wolfgang Petersen
      </a>
      . To this day, Munich remains one of the centres of the German film and entertainment industry.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Hofbr.C3.A4uhaus_and_Oktoberfest">
       Hofbruhaus and Oktoberfest
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Hofbruhaus and Oktoberfest">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">
       Oktoberfest
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BeergartenenMunich.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="800" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/BeergartenenMunich.jpg/220px-BeergartenenMunich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/BeergartenenMunich.jpg/330px-BeergartenenMunich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/7f/BeergartenenMunich.jpg/440px-BeergartenenMunich.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BeergartenenMunich.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofbr%C3%A4uhaus" title="Hofbruhaus">
         Hofbruhaus
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oktoberfest1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Oktoberfest1.jpg/220px-Oktoberfest1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Oktoberfest1.jpg/330px-Oktoberfest1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Oktoberfest1.jpg/440px-Oktoberfest1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Oktoberfest1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">
         Oktoberfest
        </a>
        (2003)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Hofbr%C3%A4uhaus_am_Platzl" title="Hofbruhaus am Platzl">
       Hofbruhaus am Platzl
      </a>
      , arguably the most famous beer hall worldwide, is located in the city centre. It also operates the second largest tent at the
      <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">
       Oktoberfest
      </a>
      , one of Munich's most famous attractions. For two weeks, the Oktoberfest attracts millions of people visiting its beer tents ("Bierzelte") and fairground attractions. The Oktoberfest was first held on 12 October 1810 in honour of the marriage of crown prince
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_I_of_Bavaria" title="Ludwig I of Bavaria">
       Ludwig
      </a>
      to Princess
      <a href="/wiki/Therese_of_Saxe-Hildburghausen" title="Therese of Saxe-Hildburghausen">
       Therese of Saxe-Hildburghausen
      </a>
      . The festivities were closed with a horse race and in the following years the horse races were continued and later developed into what is now known as the Oktoberfest. Despite its name, most of Oktoberfest occurs in September. It always finishes on the first Sunday in October unless the German national holiday on 3 October (
      <i>
       Tag der deutschen Einheit
      </i>
      , i.e., "
      <a href="/wiki/German_Unity_Day" title="German Unity Day">
       Day of German Unity
      </a>
      ") is a Monday or Tuesdaythen the Oktoberfest remains open for these days.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Culinary_specialities">
       Culinary specialities
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Culinary specialities">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Weisswurst.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1088" data-file-width="1175" height="204" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Weisswurst.jpg/220px-Weisswurst.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Weisswurst.jpg/330px-Weisswurst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Weisswurst.jpg/440px-Weisswurst.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Weisswurst.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Weisswurst" title="Weisswurst">
         <i>
          Weisswrste
         </i>
        </a>
        with
        <i>
         ser Senf
        </i>
        (sweet
        <a href="/wiki/Mustard_(condiment)" title="Mustard (condiment)">
         mustard
        </a>
        ) and a
        <i>
         Breze
        </i>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Pretzel" title="Pretzel">
         pretzel
        </a>
        )
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Weisswurst" title="Weisswurst">
       <i>
        Weiwurst
       </i>
      </a>
      ('white sausage') is a Munich speciality. Traditionally eaten only before noona tradition dating to a time before refrigeratorsthese morsels are often served with
      <i>
       sweet mustard
      </i>
      (another Munich/Bavarian specialty) and freshly baked
      <a href="/wiki/Pretzel" title="Pretzel">
       pretzels
      </a>
      . The skin has to be removed before the meat can be eaten, and to accomplish this as elegantly as possible is considered an art form in itself.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Leberk%C3%A4se" title="Leberkse">
       <i>
        Leberks
       </i>
      </a>
      , Bavarian baked sausage loaf, often served with potato salad and sometimes topped with a fried egg, is another delicacy of the region. A thick slice of it in a bun, called
      <i>
       Leberkssemmel
      </i>
      , is sold as a cheap snack in almost every butcher's shop of the city.
      <i>
       Fleischpflanzerl
      </i>
      is the Bavarian variety of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Frikadeller" title="Frikadeller">
        Frikadeller
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      <a class="extiw" href="//de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schweinsbraten" title="de:Schweinsbraten">
       <i>
        Schweinsbraten
       </i>
      </a>
      (pot roasted pork) with
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kn%C3%B6del" title="Kndel">
        Kndel
       </a>
      </i>
      (dumplings made from potatoes or white bread) and
      <a class="extiw" href="//de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Krautsalat" title="de:Krautsalat">
       <i>
        Krautsalat
       </i>
      </a>
      (a salad of white cabbage made with oil and vinegar, not to be confused with Sauerkraut) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Schweinshaxe" title="Schweinshaxe">
        Schweinshaxe
       </a>
      </i>
      (grilled pork knuckle) are the most typical heavy dishes in restaurants and beer gardens. A
      <i>
       halbe Ente
      </i>
      (roasted duck, literally "half of a duck") with
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kn%C3%B6del" title="Kndel">
        Kndel
       </a>
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Apfelrotkraut
      </i>
      (red cabbage with apple chunks) is especially popular in the colder months.
      <i>
       Saures Lngerl
      </i>
      (less commonly called
      <i>
       Beuscherl
      </i>
      ), a plate of lung, heart and spleen is also served with dumplings.
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schlachtplatte" title="Schlachtplatte">
        Schlachtplatte
       </a>
      </i>
      (literally "slaughter plate") consists of
      <i>
       Kesselfleisch
      </i>
      (boiled pork), fresh
      <i>
       Blutwurst
      </i>
      (blood sausage),
      <i>
       Leberwurst
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Liverwurst" title="Liverwurst">
       liverwurst
      </a>
      ) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">
        Sauerkraut
       </a>
      </i>
      . Traditionally only eaten on slaughtering day, it is available at any time now in restaurants. A common dish made with beef, onions and a thick dark sauce is
      <i>
       Zwiebelrostbraten
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The most famous soup might be the
      <i>
       Leberkndel
      </i>
      soup. A
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Leberkn%C3%B6del" title="Leberkndel">
        Leberkndel
       </a>
      </i>
      is a bread dumpling seasoned with liver and onions.
     </p>
     <p>
      Popular desserts include
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Apple_strudel" title="Apple strudel">
        Apfelstrudel
       </a>
      </i>
      (apple strudel) with vanilla sauce,
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Millirahmstrudel" title="Millirahmstrudel">
        Millirahmstrudel
       </a>
      </i>
      (a cream cheese strudel),
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dampfnudeln" title="Dampfnudeln">
        Dampfnudeln
       </a>
      </i>
      (yeast dumplings served with custard) and
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kniek%C3%BCchle" title="Kniekchle">
        Auszogene
       </a>
      </i>
      , a fried pastry shaped like a large doughnut without a hole. One of the most famous specialties is the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Prinzregententorte" title="Prinzregententorte">
        Prinzregententorte
       </a>
      </i>
      created in honour of the 19th-century prince regent
      <a href="/wiki/Luitpold,_Prince_Regent_of_Bavaria" title="Luitpold, Prince Regent of Bavaria">
       Luitpold
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Some specialities are typical cold dishes served in
      <a href="/wiki/Beer_garden" title="Beer garden">
       beer gardens
      </a>
      :
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Obatzda" title="Obatzda">
        Obatzda
       </a>
      </i>
      is a Bavarian cheese delicacy, a savoury blend of smashed mellow camembert prepared with cream cheese, cut onions and spicy paprika (and sometimes some butter). It is often served in the beer gardens along with
      <i>
       Radi
      </i>
      , white radish cut in thin slices and salted, and
      <i>
       Mnchner
       <a href="/wiki/Wurstsalat" title="Wurstsalat">
        Wurstsalat
       </a>
      </i>
      , Munich's famous sausage salad with thinly sliced Knackwurst marinated in vinegar and oil with onions on a bed of lettuce. Popular grilled meals include
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Steckerlfisch" title="Steckerlfisch">
        Steckerlfisch
       </a>
      </i>
      , which is usually
      <a href="/wiki/Mackerel" title="Mackerel">
       mackerel
      </a>
      , but may also be a local fish, such as brown trout or whitefish, speared on a wooden stick, grilled and smoked on charcoalthe typical feature is the crispy skin. Another classic is
      <i>
       a hoibs
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hendl" title="Hendl">
        Hendl
       </a>
      </i>
      (half a grilled chicken). A
      <i>
       Mass
      </i>
      (die
      <a href="/wiki/Ma%C3%9F" title="Ma">
       Ma
      </a>
      ) is a litre of beer, a
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radler" title="Radler">
        Radler
       </a>
      </i>
      consists of half beer and half lemonade.
      <i>
       Spezi
      </i>
      is an extremely popular non-alcoholic drink made of cola and orange lemonade.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Beers_and_breweries">
       Beers and breweries
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Beers and breweries">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Munich is famous for its breweries and the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weissbier" title="Weissbier">
        Weissbier
       </a>
      </i>
      (or
      <i>
       Weizenbier
      </i>
      , wheat beer) is a speciality from Bavaria.
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pale_lager" title="Pale lager">
        Helles
       </a>
      </i>
      with its translucent gold colour is the most popular Munich beer today, although it's not old (only introduced in 1895) and is the result of a change in beer tastes. Helles has largely replaced the
      <i>
       Munich Dark Beer
      </i>
      (
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Dunkel" title="Dunkel">
        Dunkles
       </a>
      </i>
      ), which gets its dark colour from burnt malt. It was the typical beer in Munich in the 19th century, but today it is more of a specialty.
      <i>
       Starkbier
      </i>
      is the strongest Munich beer, containing 69 percent alcohol. It is dark amber in color and has a heavy malty taste. It is available and popular during the Lenten
      <i>
       Starkbierzeit
      </i>
      (strong beer season), which begins on or before St. Joseph's Day (19 March). The beer served at
      <a href="/wiki/Oktoberfest" title="Oktoberfest">
       Oktoberfest
      </a>
      is a special type of
      <i>
       Mrzen
      </i>
      beer with a higher alcohol content than regular Helles.
     </p>
     <p>
      There are countless
      <i>
       Wirtshuser
      </i>
      (traditional Bavarian ale houses/restaurants) all over the city area, many of which also have small outside areas.
      <i>
       Biergrten
      </i>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Beer_garden" title="Beer garden">
       beer gardens
      </a>
      ) are the most famous and popular fixtures of Munich's gastronomic landscape. They are central to the city's culture and serve as a kind of melting pot for members of all walks of life, for locals, expatriates and tourists alike. It is allowed to bring one's own food to a beer garden. There are many smaller beer gardens and around 20 major ones, providing at least one thousand seats, with four of the most famous and popular being located in the
      <a href="/wiki/Englischer_Garten" title="Englischer Garten">
       Englischer Garten
      </a>
      :
      <i>
       Chinesischer Turm
      </i>
      (Munich's second largest beergarden with 7000 seats),
      <i>
       Seehaus
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Hirschau
      </i>
      and
      <i>
       Aumeister
      </i>
      . Among locals, connoisseurs and well-informed tourists,
      <i>
       Augustiner-Keller
      </i>
      , located near
      <i>
       Hauptbahnhof
      </i>
      (central station) at
      <i>
       Arnulfstrae
      </i>
      , is one of the most popular beergarden of the city, since it is the only one in which Munich's most popular beer,
      <i>
       Augustiner
      </i>
      , is pulled from wooden barrels.
      <i>
       Nockherberg
      </i>
      ,
      <i>
       Hofbrukeller
      </i>
      (not to be confused with the
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofbr%C3%A4uhaus" title="Hofbruhaus">
        Hofbruhaus
       </a>
      </i>
      ) and
      <i>
       Lwenbrukeller
      </i>
      are other famous beergardens.
      <i>
       Hirschgarten
      </i>
      is the largest beer garden in the world with 8000 seats.
     </p>
     <p>
      There are six breweries in Munich:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Augustiner-Br%C3%A4u" title="Augustiner-Bru">
        Augustiner-Bru
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Hacker-Pschorr_Brewery" title="Hacker-Pschorr Brewery">
        Hacker-Pschorr
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hofbr%C3%A4uhaus" title="Hofbruhaus">
        Hofbru
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/L%C3%B6wenbr%C3%A4u" title="Lwenbru">
        Lwenbru
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paulaner" title="Paulaner">
        Paulaner
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Spaten-Franziskaner-Br%C3%A4u" title="Spaten-Franziskaner-Bru">
        Spaten-Franziskaner-Bru
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Markets">
       Markets
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Markets">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Viktualienmarkt" title="Viktualienmarkt">
        Viktualienmarkt
       </a>
      </i>
      is Munich's most popular market for fresh food and delicatessen. A very old feature of Munich's Fasching (carnival) is the dance of the Marktfrauen (market women) of the Viktualienmarkt in comical costumes.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Auer_Dult" title="Auer Dult">
        Auer Dult
       </a>
      </i>
      is held three times a year on the square around Mariahilf church and is one of Munich's oldest markets, well known for its hardware, trinkets and antiques.
     </p>
     <p>
      Three weeks before Christmas the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Christmas_market" title="Christmas market">
        Christkindlmarkt
       </a>
      </i>
      opens at Marienplatz and other squares in the city, selling Christmas goods.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Nightlife">
       Nightlife
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Nightlife">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Nightlife" title="Nightlife">
       Nightlife
      </a>
      in Munich is located mostly in the city centre (
      <a href="/wiki/Altstadt-Lehel" title="Altstadt-Lehel">
       Altstadt-Lehel
      </a>
      ) and the boroughs
      <a href="/wiki/Maxvorstadt" title="Maxvorstadt">
       Maxvorstadt
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt" title="Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt">
       Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Au-Haidhausen" title="Au-Haidhausen">
       Au-Haidhausen
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">
       Schwabing
      </a>
      . Between
      <a href="/wiki/Sendlinger_Tor" title="Sendlinger Tor">
       Sendlinger Tor
      </a>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maximilansplatz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maximilansplatz (page does not exist)">
       Maximilansplatz
      </a>
      lies the so-called Feierbanane (party banana), a roughly banana-shaped unofficial party zone spanning 1.3km along Sonnenstrae, characterized by a high concentration of clubs, bars and restaurants. In recent years, the Feierbanane has become the mainstream focus of Munich's nightlife and tends to get quite crowded, especially on weekends. It also has sparked some debate among city officials regarding alcohol-related security issues and the party zone's general impact on local residents as well as day-time businesses.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt" title="Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt">
       Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt
      </a>
      's two main quarters, Grtnerplatzviertel and Glockenbachviertel, are both considered decidedly less mainstream than most other nightlife hotspots in the city and are renowned for their many hip and laid back bars and clubs as well as for being Munich's main centers of gay culture. On warm spring or summer nights, hundreds of young people can be seen gathering at Grtnerplatz, where they lay down in the grass to relax, talk with friends and drink beer, occupying most of the square's available space in the process.
      <a href="/wiki/Maxvorstadt" title="Maxvorstadt">
       Maxvorstadt
      </a>
      has many smaller bars that are especially popular with university students, whereas legendary
      <a href="/wiki/Schwabing" title="Schwabing">
       Schwabing
      </a>
      , once Munich's first and foremost party district, has lost much of its nightlife activity in the last few decades, mainly due to gentrification and the resulting extraordinarily high rents (even for Munich standards). It has become the city's most coveted (and one of its most expensive) residential districts, attracting affluent citizens with little interest in partying. Nevertheless, some of its more excentric aspects have survived, and there are still a few legendary venues like the underground
      <a href="/wiki/Schwabinger_7" title="Schwabinger 7">
       Schwabinger 7
      </a>
      and live clubs such as Schwabinger Podium.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Kultfabrik, a former industrial complex that was converted to a large party area near
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Ostbahnhof" title="Mnchen Ostbahnhof">
       Mnchen Ostbahnhof
      </a>
      in Haidhausen, hosts more than 25 clubs and is especially popular among younger people and/or residents of the metropolitan area surrounding Munich. Apart from the Kultfarbik and its smaller cousin Optimolwerke, there exists a wide variety of establishments in the more urban parts of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Haidhausen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Haidhausen (page does not exist)">
       Haidhausen
      </a>
      . Generally speaking, Munich nightlife tends to change quite dramatically over very short periods of time. Establishments are opening and closing every year, with some surviving only a few months, while others can last for many years. Within recent history, Munich has had a few musical venues that have made more of an impact than others, some even gaining international recognition, such as Big Apple, PN, Tanzlokal Grenwahn, Atomic Cafe, Ultraschall or Babalu Bar, to name a few. Munich has two directly connected gay quarters, which basically can be seen as one: Grtnerplatzviertel and Glockenbachviertel, both part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt" title="Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt">
       Ludwigsvorstadt-Isarvorstadt
      </a>
      district.
     </p>
     <p>
      Some notable establishments are:
     </p>
     <p>
      Bars (Pubs are located all over the city):
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Schumann's - Charles Schumann's Cocktail Bar
      </li>
      <li>
       Havana Club
      </li>
      <li>
       Bar Centrale
      </li>
      <li>
       Holy Home
      </li>
      <li>
       Eat the Rich
      </li>
      <li>
       Pimpernel
      </li>
      <li>
       M.C. Mueller
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Clubs:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       P1 - Favourite meeting place of Munich's High Society, the so-called
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Schickeria&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Schickeria (page does not exist)">
        Schickeria
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       Harry Klein
      </li>
      <li>
       EdMoses
      </li>
      <li>
       Rote Sonne
      </li>
      <li>
       Call me Drella
      </li>
      <li>
       Cord
      </li>
      <li>
       M.C. Mueller
      </li>
      <li>
       Backstage - catering to more alternative and rock tastes.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      Munich has more than 100 night clubs and thousands of bars and restaurants within city limits.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Circus">
       Circus
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Circus">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Circus_Krone" title="Circus Krone">
       Circus Krone
      </a>
      is based in Munich and one of the largest circus in Europe.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was the first and still is one of only a few in Western Europe to also occupy a
      <a href="/wiki/Circus_Krone_Building" title="Circus Krone Building">
       building
      </a>
      of its own.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges_and_universities">
       Colleges and universities
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Colleges and universities">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Munich is a leading location for science and research with a long list of Nobel Prize laureates from
      <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_R%C3%B6ntgen" title="Wilhelm Rntgen">
       Wilhelm Conrad Rntgen
      </a>
      in 1901 to
      <a href="/wiki/Theodor_W._H%C3%A4nsch" title="Theodor W. Hnsch">
       Theodor Hnsch
      </a>
      in 2005. Munich has become a spiritual centre already since the times of Emperor Louis IV when philosophers like
      <a href="/wiki/Michael_of_Cesena" title="Michael of Cesena">
       Michael of Cesena
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Marsilius_of_Padua" title="Marsilius of Padua">
       Marsilius of Padua
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/William_of_Ockham" title="William of Ockham">
       William of Ockham
      </a>
      were protected at the emperor's court. The Ludwig Maximilian University (LMU) and the Technische Universitt Mnchen (TU or TUM), were two of the first three German universities to be awarded the title
      <i>
       elite university
      </i>
      by a selection committee composed of academics and members of the Ministries of Education and Research of the Federation and the German states (Lnder). Only the two Munich universities and the Technical University of Karlsruhe (now part of
      <a href="/wiki/Karlsruhe_Institute_of_Technology" title="Karlsruhe Institute of Technology">
       Karlsruhe Institute of Technology
      </a>
      ) have held this honour, and the implied greater chances of attracting research funds, since the first evaluation round in 2006.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ludwig-Maximilians-Universit%C3%A4t_M%C3%BCnchen.jpg">

       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
