     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_research_institutions">
       Scientific research institutions
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Scientific research institutions">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Max_Planck_Society">
       Max Planck Society
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Max Planck Society">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Society" title="Max Planck Society">
       Max Planck Society
      </a>
      , an independent German non-profit research organization, has its administrative headquarters in Munich. The following institutes are located in the Munich area:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Astrophysics" title="Max Planck Institute for Astrophysics">
        Max Planck Institute for Astrophysics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Garching_bei_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Garching bei Mnchen">
        Garching
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_of_Biochemistry" title="Max Planck Institute of Biochemistry">
        Max Planck Institute of Biochemistry
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Martinsried" title="Martinsried">
        Martinsried
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Extraterrestrial_Physics" title="Max Planck Institute for Extraterrestrial Physics">
        Max Planck Institute for Extraterrestrial Physics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Garching_bei_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Garching bei Mnchen">
        Garching
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Foreign_and_International_Social_Law" title="Max Planck Institute for Foreign and International Social Law">
        Max Planck Institute for Foreign and International Social Law
       </a>
       , Mnchen
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Intellectual_Property,_Competition_and_Tax_Law" title="Max Planck Institute for Intellectual Property, Competition and Tax Law">
        Max Planck Institute for Intellectual Property, Competition and Tax Law
       </a>
       , Mnchen
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_of_Neurobiology" title="Max Planck Institute of Neurobiology">
        Max Planck Institute of Neurobiology
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Martinsried" title="Martinsried">
        Martinsried
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Max_Planck_Institute_for_Ornithology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Max Planck Institute for Ornithology (page does not exist)">
        Max Planck Institute for Ornithology
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Andechs" title="Andechs">
        Andechs
       </a>
       -
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Erling,_Germany&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Erling, Germany (page does not exist)">
        Erling
       </a>
       (Biological Rhythms and Behaviour),
       <a href="/wiki/Radolfzell" title="Radolfzell">
        Radolfzell
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Seewiesen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Seewiesen (page does not exist)">
        Seewiesen
       </a>
       (Reproductive Biology and Behaviour)
       <a class="external autonumber" href="http://www.orn.mpg.de/" rel="nofollow">
        [6]
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Physics" title="Max Planck Institute for Physics">
        Max Planck Institute for Physics
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Physics" title="Max Planck Institute for Physics">
        Werner Heisenberg Institute
       </a>
       ), Mnchen
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Max-Planck-Institut_f%C3%BCr_Plasmaphysik" title="Max-Planck-Institut fr Plasmaphysik">
        Max Planck Institute for Plasma Physics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Garching_bei_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Garching bei Mnchen">
        Garching
       </a>
       (also in
       <a href="/wiki/Greifswald" title="Greifswald">
        Greifswald
       </a>
       )
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_of_Psychiatry" title="Max Planck Institute of Psychiatry">
        Max Planck Institute of Psychiatry
       </a>
       , Mnchen
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_for_Psychological_Research" title="Max Planck Institute for Psychological Research">
        Max Planck Institute for Psychological Research
       </a>
       , Mnchen (closed)
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Max_Planck_Institute_of_Quantum_Optics" title="Max Planck Institute of Quantum Optics">
        Max Planck Institute of Quantum Optics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Garching_bei_M%C3%BCnchen" title="Garching bei Mnchen">
        Garching
       </a>
      </li>
     </ul>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
       Economy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Economy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BMW_building_munich.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="852" data-file-width="1182" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BMW_building_munich.jpg/220px-BMW_building_munich.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BMW_building_munich.jpg/330px-BMW_building_munich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/BMW_building_munich.jpg/440px-BMW_building_munich.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BMW_building_munich.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/BMW_Headquarters" title="BMW Headquarters">
         BMW Headquarters
        </a>
        building (one of the few buildings that have been built from the top to the bottom) and the bowl shaped BMW museum
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Siemens_Palais.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2088" data-file-width="3608" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Siemens_Palais.JPG/220px-Siemens_Palais.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Siemens_Palais.JPG/330px-Siemens_Palais.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Siemens_Palais.JPG/440px-Siemens_Palais.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Siemens_Palais.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Munich headquarters of
        <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">
         Siemens
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich has the strongest economy of any German city
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the lowest unemployment rate (3.0% in June 2014) of any German city with more than a million people (the others being Berlin, Hamburg and
      <a href="/wiki/Cologne" title="Cologne">
       Cologne
      </a>
      ).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
       <a href="#cite_note-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The city is also the economic centre of
      <a href="/wiki/Southern_Germany" title="Southern Germany">
       southern Germany
      </a>
      . The initiative "Neue Soziale Marktwirtschaft (INSM)" (New Social Market Economy) and the "
      <a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswoche" title="Wirtschaftswoche">
       WirtschaftsWoche
      </a>
      " (Business Weekly) magazine awarded Munich the top score in their comparative survey for the third time in June 2006. Munich topped the ranking of the magazine "Capital" in February 2005 for the economic prospects between 2002 and 2011 in sixty German cities. Munich is a
      <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">
       Financial centre
      </a>
      and a
      <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">
       Global city
      </a>
      and holds the headquarters of
      <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">
       Siemens AG
      </a>
      (electronics),
      <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">
       BMW
      </a>
      (car),
      <a href="/wiki/MAN_SE" title="MAN SE">
       MAN AG
      </a>
      (truck manufacturer, engineering),
      <a href="/wiki/The_Linde_Group" title="The Linde Group">
       Linde
      </a>
      (gases),
      <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">
       Allianz
      </a>
      (insurance),
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Re" title="Munich Re">
       Munich Re
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Reinsurance" title="Reinsurance">
       re-insurance
      </a>
      ), and
      <a href="/wiki/Rohde_%26_Schwarz" title="Rohde &amp; Schwarz">
       Rohde &amp; Schwarz
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">
       electronics
      </a>
      ). Among German cities with more than 500,000 inhabitants purchasing power is highest in Munich (26,648 euro per inhabitant) as of 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2006, Munich blue-collar workers enjoyed an average hourly wage of 18.62 euro (ca. $23).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The breakdown by cities proper (not metropolitan areas) of
      <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">
       Global 500 cities
      </a>
      listed Munich in 8th position in 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Munich is also a centre for
      <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">
       biotechnology
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Software" title="Software">
       software
      </a>
      and other
      <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">
       service industries
      </a>
      . Munich is also the home of the headquarters of many other large companies such as the aircraft engine manufacturer
      <a href="/wiki/MTU_Aero_Engines" title="MTU Aero Engines">
       MTU Aero Engines
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Injection_molding_machine" title="Injection molding machine">
       injection molding machine
      </a>
      manufacturer
      <a href="/wiki/Krauss-Maffei" title="Krauss-Maffei">
       Krauss-Maffei
      </a>
      , the camera and lighting manufacturer
      <a href="/wiki/Arri" title="Arri">
       Arri
      </a>
      , the semiconductor firm
      <a href="/wiki/Infineon_Technologies" title="Infineon Technologies">
       Infineon Technologies
      </a>
      (headquartered in the suburban town of
      <a href="/wiki/Neubiberg" title="Neubiberg">
       Neubiberg
      </a>
      ), lighting giant
      <a href="/wiki/Osram" title="Osram">
       Osram
      </a>
      , as well as the German or European headquarters of many foreign companies such as
      <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">
       McDonald's
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">
       Microsoft
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Munich has significance as a
      <a href="/wiki/Munich%27s_financial_community" title="Munich's financial community">
       financial centre
      </a>
      (second only to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Frankfurt am Main">
       Frankfurt
      </a>
      ), being home of
      <a href="/wiki/HypoVereinsbank" title="HypoVereinsbank">
       HypoVereinsbank
      </a>
      and the Bayerische Landesbank. It outranks
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Frankfurt am Main">
       Frankfurt
      </a>
      though as home of insurance companies such as
      <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">
       Allianz
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Re" title="Munich Re">
       Munich Re
      </a>
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2013)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Munich is the largest publishing city in Europe
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and home to
      <a href="/wiki/S%C3%BCddeutsche_Zeitung" title="Sddeutsche Zeitung">
       Sddeutsche Zeitung
      </a>
      , one of Germany's largest daily newspapers. The city is also the location of the programming headquarters of Germany's largest public broadcasting network,
      <a href="/wiki/ARD_(broadcaster)" title="ARD (broadcaster)">
       ARD
      </a>
      , while the largest commercial network,
      <a href="/wiki/ProSieben" title="ProSieben">
       Pro7-Sat1 Media AG
      </a>
      , is headquartered in the suburb of
      <a href="/wiki/Unterf%C3%B6hring" title="Unterfhring">
       Unterfhring
      </a>
      . The headquarters of the German branch of
      <a href="/wiki/Random_House" title="Random House">
       Random House
      </a>
      , the world's largest publishing house, and of
      <a href="/wiki/Hubert_Burda_Media" title="Hubert Burda Media">
       Burda publishing group
      </a>
      are also in Munich.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bavaria_Film_Studios" title="Bavaria Film Studios">
       Bavaria Film Studios
      </a>
      are located in the suburb of
      <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnwald,_Bavaria" title="Grnwald, Bavaria">
       Grnwald
      </a>
      . They are one of Europe's biggest and most famous film production studios.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>

        <span>

       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
       Transportation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Transportation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2394" data-file-width="3215" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png/300px-Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png/450px-Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png/600px-Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png 2x" width="300"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Verkehrsnetz_M%C3%BCnchen.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Public transport network
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Munich_International_Airport">
       Munich International Airport
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Munich International Airport">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">
       Franz Josef Strauss International Airport
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">
       IATA
      </a>
      : MUC,
      <a href="/wiki/International_Civil_Aviation_Organization" title="International Civil Aviation Organization">
       ICAO
      </a>
      : EDDM) is the second-largest airport in Germany and seventh-largest in Europe after
      <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" title="London Heathrow Airport">
       London Heathrow
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport">
       Paris Charle de Gaulle
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_International_Airport" title="Frankfurt International Airport">
       Frankfurt
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">
       Amsterdam
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barajas_Airport" title="Barajas Airport">
       Madrid
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atat%C3%BCrk_International_Airport" title="Atatrk International Airport">
       Istanbul Atatrk
      </a>
      . It is used by about 34 million passengers a year, and lies some 30km (19mi) north east of the city centre. It replaced the smaller
      <a href="/wiki/Munich-Riem_Airport" title="Munich-Riem Airport">
       Munich-Riem airport
      </a>
      in 1992. The airport can be reached by suburban train lines
      <b>
       S8
      </b>
      from the east and
      <b>
       S1
      </b>
      from the west of the city. From the
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hauptbahnhof" title="Mnchen Hauptbahnhof">
       main railway station
      </a>
      the journey takes 4045 minutes. An express train will be added that will cut down travel time to 2025 minutes with limited stops on dedicated tracks. A
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maglev_(transport)" title="Maglev (transport)">
       magnetic levitation train
      </a>
      (called
      <a href="/wiki/Transrapid" title="Transrapid">
       Transrapid
      </a>
      ), which was to have run at speeds of up to 400km/h (249mph) from the central station to the airport in a travel time of 10 minutes, had been approved,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but was cancelled in March 2008 because of cost escalation and after heavy protests.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
       <a href="#cite_note-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">
       Lufthansa
      </a>
      opened its second hub at the airport when Terminal 2 was opened in 2003.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_airports">
       Other airports
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Other airports">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      In 2008, the Bavarian state government granted a license to expand
      <i>
       Oberpfaffenhofen Air Station
      </i>
      located west of Munich, for commercial use. These plans were opposed by many residents in the Oberpfaffenhofen area as well as other branches of local Government, including the city of Munich, which took the case to court.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, in October 2009, the permit allowing up to 9725 business flights per year to depart from or land at Oberpfaffenhofen was confirmed by a regional judge.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite being 110km (68mi) from Munich,
      <a href="/wiki/Memmingen_Airport" title="Memmingen Airport">
       Memmingen Airport
      </a>
      has been advertised as
      <i>
       Airport Munich West
      </i>
      . After 2005, passenger traffic of nearby
      <a href="/wiki/Augsburg_Airport" title="Augsburg Airport">
       Augsburg Airport
      </a>
      was relocated to Munich Airport, leaving the Augsburg region of Bavaria without an air passenger airport within close reach.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">
       Public transportation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Public transportation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="4695" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG/220px-Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG/330px-Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG/440px-Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Westfriedhof_zentral.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        <a href="/wiki/Westfriedhof_(Munich_U-Bahn)" title="Westfriedhof (Munich U-Bahn)">
         Westfriedhof platform
        </a>
        of the
        <a href="/wiki/Munich_U-Bahn" title="Munich U-Bahn">
         Munich U-Bahn
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      For its urban population of 2.6million people, Munich and its closest suburbs have one of the most comprehensive and punctual systems in the world, incorporating the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_U-Bahn" title="Munich U-Bahn">
       Munich U-Bahn (underground railway)
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_S-Bahn" title="Munich S-Bahn">
       Munich S-Bahn (suburban trains)
      </a>
      , trams and buses. The system is supervised by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munich_Transport_and_Tariff_Association" title="Munich Transport and Tariff Association">
       Munich Transport and Tariff Association
      </a>
      (
      <i>
       Mnchner Verkehrs- und Tarifverbund
       <a href="/wiki/Gesellschaft_mit_beschr%C3%A4nkter_Haftung" title="Gesellschaft mit beschrnkter Haftung">
        GmbH
       </a>
      </i>
      ). The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munich_tramway" title="Munich tramway">
       Munich tramway
      </a>
      is the oldest existing public transportation system in the city, which has been in operation since 1876. Munich also has an extensive network of bus lines.
     </p>
     <p>
      The extensive network of subway and tram lines assist and complement pedestrian movement in the city centre. The 700m-long Kaufinger Strasse, which starts near the Main train station, forms a pedestrian east-west spine that traverses almost the entire centre. Similarly, Weinstrasse leads off northwards to the Hofgarten. These major spines and many smaller streets cover an extensive area of the centre that can be enjoyed on foot and bike. The transformation of the historic area into a pedestrian priority zone enables and invites walking and biking by making these active modes of transport comfortable, safe and enjoyable. These attributes result from applying the principle of
      <a href="/wiki/Permeability_(spatial_and_transport_planning)" title="Permeability (spatial and transport planning)">
       "filtered permability"
      </a>
      which selectively restricts the number of roads that run through the centre. While certain streets are discontinuous for cars, they connect to a network of pedestrian and bike paths which permeate the entire centre. In addition, these paths go through public squares and open spaces increasing the enjoyment of the trip(see image). The logic of filtering a mode of transport is fully expressed in a comprehensive model for laying out neighbourhoods and districtsthe
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fused_Grid" title="Fused Grid">
       Fused Grid
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      The main railway station is
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Hauptbahnhof" title="Mnchen Hauptbahnhof">
       Munich Hauptbahnhof
      </a>
      , in the city centre, and there are two smaller main line stations at
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen-Pasing_station" title="Mnchen-Pasing station">
       Pasing
      </a>
      , in the west of the city, and
      <a href="/wiki/M%C3%BCnchen_Ost_station" title="Mnchen Ost station">
       Munich Ostbahnhof
      </a>
      in the east. All three are connected to the public transport system and serve as transportation hubs.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Intercity-Express" title="Intercity-Express">
       ICE highspeed trains
      </a>
      stop at Munich-Pasing and Munich-Hauptbahnhof only.
      <a href="/wiki/InterCity" title="InterCity">
       InterCity
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/EuroCity" title="EuroCity">
       EuroCity
      </a>
      trains to destinations east of Munich also stop at Munich East. Since 28 May 2006 Munich has been connected to
      <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">
       Nuremberg
      </a>
      via
      <a href="/wiki/Ingolstadt" title="Ingolstadt">
       Ingolstadt
      </a>
      by the 300km/h (186mph)
      <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg%E2%80%93Munich_high-speed_railway" title="NurembergMunich high-speed railway">
       NurembergMunich high-speed railway
      </a>
      line.
     </p>
     <p>
      The trade fair
      <a href="/wiki/Transport_Logistic" title="Transport Logistic">
       transport logistic
      </a>
      is held every two years at the
      <i>
       Neue Messe Mnchen
      </i>
      (Messe Mnchen International).
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Individual_transportation">
       Individual transportation
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Individual transportation">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2211" data-file-width="2473" height="197" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png/220px-Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png/330px-Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png/440px-Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Karte_Fernstra%C3%9Fen_M%C3%BCnchen.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Munich
        <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">
         motorway
        </a>
        network
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3072" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg/220px-Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg/330px-Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg/440px-Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Munich_-_Maria_column_05.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The Mariensule (Mary's column)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Munich is an integral part of the
      <a href="/wiki/Autobahn" title="Autobahn">
       motorway
      </a>
      network of southern Germany. Motorways from
      <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">
       Stuttgart
      </a>
      (W),
      <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg" title="Nuremberg">
       Nuremberg
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Frankfurt_am_Main" title="Frankfurt am Main">
       Frankfurt
      </a>
      and Berlin (N),
      <a href="/wiki/Deggendorf" title="Deggendorf">
       Deggendorf
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Passau" title="Passau">
       Passau
      </a>
      (E),
      <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">
       Salzburg
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Innsbruck" title="Innsbruck">
       Innsbruck
      </a>
      (SE),
      <a href="/wiki/Garmisch-Partenkirchen" title="Garmisch-Partenkirchen">
       Garmisch Partenkirchen
      </a>
      (S) and
      <a href="/wiki/Lindau" title="Lindau">
       Lindau
      </a>
      (SW) terminate at Munich, allowing direct access to the different parts of Germany, Austria and Italy.
     </p>
     <p>
      Traffic is however, often very heavy in and around Munich. Traffic jams are commonplace during rush hour and at the beginning and end of major holidays in Germany, in no small part due to poor traffic light changing patterns and synchronisation. There are few "green waves" or roundabouts. Another contributing factor is the lack of a proper ring road. This
      <i>
       mittlere Ring
      </i>
      is a ring road in name only and is a loosely connected system of roads with many traffic light controlled junctions.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">
       Cycling
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Cycling">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Cycling_in_Munich" title="Cycling in Munich">
       Cycling in Munich
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Cycling is recognised as a good alternative to motorised transport and the growing number of
      <a href="/wiki/Segregated_cycle_facilities" title="Segregated cycle facilities">
       bicycle lanes
      </a>
      are widely used throughout the year. They are mostly not segregated from foot paths, making them dangerous to both parties. Many of the cycle path surfaces are of poor quality often due to the roots of roadside trees breaking through the tarmac, fortunately the roads themselves are seldom affected by these tree roots. The cycle paths usually involve a longer route than by the road as they are diverted around objects and the presence of pedestrians tends to make them quite slow.
     </p>
     <p>
      A modern
      <a href="/wiki/Call_a_Bike" title="Call a Bike">
       bike hire system
      </a>
      is available within the area bounded by the
      <i>
       Mittlerer Ring
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Around_Munich">
       Around Munich
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Munich&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Around Munich">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      The Munich agglomeration sprawls across the plain of the
      <a href="/wiki/Foothills" title="Foothills">
       Alpine foothills
      </a>
      comprising about 2.6million inhabitants. Several smaller traditional Bavarian towns and cities like
      <a href="/wiki/Dachau" title="Dachau">
       Dachau
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Freising" title="Freising">
       Freising
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Erding" title="Erding">
       Erding
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Starnberg" title="Starnberg">
       Starnberg
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Landshut" title="Landshut">
       Landshut
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Moosburg" title="Moosburg">
       Moosburg
      </a>
      are today part of the Greater Munich Region, formed by Munich and the surrounding districts, making up the
      <a href="/wiki/Munich_Metropolitan_Region" title="Munich Metropolitan Region">
       Munich Metropolitan Region
      </a>
      , which has a population of about 4.5million people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
